A Land of Three Months of Perpetual Day and Three Months of Perpetual Night 83

▲ The name of a place in Northern Siberia is Igarka

▲ Once uninhabited, it is now a small city of over ten thousand people

TASS Dispatch from Moscow: The industrial and cultural influence of the Soviet Union has penetrated its northernmost borders. Areas where explorers once never set foot are now being developed and constructed. In Northern Siberia, near 67.5 degrees north latitude, there is a place called Igarka. Within the Arctic Circle, small steamers can reach it in fourteen to fifteen days during the summer when the rivers thaw. In winter, it takes two to three months by fire and dog sled to reach the area. Most strangely, the area experiences three months of the year when the sun sets and does not rise, and another three months when the sun shines continuously and does not set. During the three months of winter without sunshine, it is perpetually dark, and the temperature drops to minus 60 degrees Celsius. However, even summer is not warm, and the ground is frozen solid two feet below the surface. The area has unlimited natural resources, especially graphite, coal, and non-metallic minerals. Three years ago, the area was uninhabited. Now, after development, it has become a small city of 12,000 people, with several factories and schools. Its population includes more than thirty different ethnic groups. Newly established schools are determined to eliminate adult illiteracy first, and the cultural situation is showing signs of progress.

Hitler Replies to Hindenburg, Rejecting Conditions for Forming a Cabinet

Demands the President Grant Him Dictatorial Powers 84

Reuters Dispatch from Berlin, 23rd: Nazi Party leader Hitler today replied to President Hindenburg, rejecting the conditions for accepting the position of Chancellor. Hitler stated that because of these conditions, he could not form a government supported by a majority of the Reichstag. Hitler also suggested forming a presidential cabinet, with himself or another Nazi Party member as Chancellor, and granting him dictatorial powers so that he could dissolve the Reichstag and abolish the constitution when it became unruly. Hitler asked the President to accept his plan, because the motherland is in a state of despair, and only this can resolve the political crisis in the shortest possible time. The Nazi Party is still trying to win the support of the German National People's Party and the Stahlhelm.

Reuters Dispatch from Berlin, 24th: It is reported that President Hindenburg has rejected Hitler's proposal to form a presidential cabinet led by himself.

National News Agency Dispatch from Berlin, 23rd: Hitler's reply to Hindenburg today, which is eight pages long, has declined to form a government supported by the Reichstag and stated that he is still willing to be at the President's disposal. The President is currently studying Hitler's reply. Political circles now believe that Hitler will not be able to form a government for the time being, and the President will ask other leaders to form a new government.

Page 8

Hoover Issues Declaration Rejecting Moratorium on War Debts 85

Debtor Nations Can Repay Debts in Their Own Currency

Another Committee to Be Formed to Discuss the Entire Issue

Stimson Responds to Britain and France Based on This Principle 86

National News Agency Dispatch from Washington, 23rd: After meeting with members of Congress today, US President Hoover issued a statement on the war debt issue, giving Europe a glimmer of hope for revising the war debts. However, the revision depends on the issue of arms reduction and the World Economic Conference. If the goal is to effectively relieve the finances of debtor nations, it will be very limited, and there is no suggestion of extending the moratorium period for debts due in December, indicating a continued unwillingness to concede. However, the proposal that debtor nations may repay debts in their own currency, rather than US dollars, may slightly alleviate their suffering.

Reuters Dispatch from Washington, 24th: Secretary of State Stimson today replied to the notes from France and Britain regarding the war debt issue.

Reuters Dispatch from New York, 23rd: President Hoover's decision on war debts has caused the pound to fall to a new low for the year, at $3.24 and 7/8.

War Debts Are Related to Arms Reduction 87

National News Agency Dispatch from Washington, 23rd: President Hoover's statement is several thousand words long. Its main recommendation is that Congress should form a war debt committee to discuss the entire war debt issue with the debtor nations. The committee members should be the US representatives to the World Disarmament Conference and the World Economic Conference. In addition, before describing this proposal, he declared that the current debt agreements must be maintained (in other words, the payments due this term must be paid as scheduled).

As for the request from Britain, France, and other countries to extend the moratorium period or revise the agreement, President Hoover explained his position, saying that Britain, France, and other countries have not presented sufficient facts to prove that the debts due in December should be postponed. They only proposed suspending the payments due in December and that the two governments engage in discussions on the war debt issue, but lacked evidence of an inability to pay. In my view, this proposal is not very strong. I believe that the American people should not be asked to make further sacrifices. I must reiterate that in the minds of Americans, the war debt issue is closely related to the arms reduction issue and the heavy burden placed on Americans and other people by the competition in armaments. Therefore, we must develop an important avenue for mutual benefit.

After President Hoover's statement was released, French Ambassador Claudel went to the State Department to obtain a copy and made no comment. It is expected that representatives of the debtor nations will each receive a copy within a few hours. In addition, President-elect Roosevelt was also sent a copy by the government before departing for Warm Springs for rest and recuperation. Democratic leaders returned to the Mayflower Hotel after Hoover's declaration and consulted with Roosevelt on the matter.

Nature of the War Debt Committee 88

According to President Hoover's proposal, the formation of a war debt committee is, in effect, a re-establishment of the War Debt Funding Commission, granting it full authority to negotiate with the debtor nations and then report the results of the negotiations and its recommendations to Congress. The suggestion that committee members should be disarmament representatives and economic conference representatives can be seen as an indication that the US government will not agree to revise the war debts until Europe reduces its armaments. The suggestion that economic issues should also be included in the discussion is, in effect, only for the sake of saving time.

As for the reason for President Hoover's proposal, the meeting between Presidents Hoover and Roosevelt yesterday did not yield results, and today's consultation with members of Congress did not reach an agreement. Hoover, with his term coming to an end, did not want to shoulder the difficult task of resolving the war debt issue again, so he informally handed the entire issue over to Congress. It is expected that when Congress convenes in the future, the President will formally propose this in his report on the state of the union. As for President Hoover's previous expression of support for extending the moratorium period and his sudden change of attitude this time, it is because members of Congress largely opposed extending the moratorium period.

The situation during today's meeting between the President and members of Congress can be described as not very fruitful. Afterwards, Republican Senator Watson told people, "None of us agreed." Democratic leader Rayburn stated, "We agreed with the President on two points: that war debts should not be reduced or canceled again, and that the payments due in December should be paid as scheduled." Senator Harrison stated that members of Congress had little enthusiasm for the war debt committee proposal.

After today's meeting between the President and members of Congress, financier Bernard Baruch went to invite Roosevelt to meet with President Hoover again, but Roosevelt politely declined. Afterwards, Roosevelt met with Democratic members of Congress at the Mayflower Hotel and then left for Warm Springs for rest and recuperation. The details of the Democratic leaders' meeting have not been released.

Roosevelt Expresses His Opinion 89

Later, Roosevelt expressed his opinion on the train, saying that the war debt issue between the United States and European countries can be negotiated by existing diplomatic agencies and does not need to be handled by Congress or a separate committee. He also said that he and President Hoover had many points of agreement on the war debt issue, but that he firmly insisted during his meeting with the President that the request from Britain, France, and other countries to suspend the payments due in December was a matter for the current government. He also said that the two completely agreed that the actual amount borrowed must be repaid, and that debtor nations must negotiate separately with the United States, not hold a general meeting where debtor nations and creditor nations stand on opposite sides, because he and President Hoover both believe that such negotiations should be handled separately based on each country's economic situation and ability to pay. Also, the war debt issue must be completely separated from the German reparations issue. The United States will only begin negotiations with the debtor nations after this is clearly stated.

Britain and France Experience Painful Reactions 90

National News Agency Dispatch from London, 24th: After the news that the US government firmly refused to make concessions on war debts reached here, it immediately made a deep impression on the British government and public. Because the news arrived too late last night, the cabinet did not meet, but it was reported that the Chancellor of the Exchequer immediately prepared a new draft note, which will be submitted to the cabinet for discussion today and sent to Washington. News from New York reported that Morgan is willing to lend Britain £20 million to maintain the pound, with an equal amount of gold stored in London as collateral, but British financial circles are not very enthusiastic about this. If Morgan's loan proposal is indeed in the aforementioned manner, it is feared that it may not be accepted by Britain.

National News Agency Dispatch from London, 24th: Since the US rejected Britain's proposal to suspend war debt payments, the exchange rate between the British pound and the US dollar opened this morning, immediately falling from 3.273125 at yesterday's close to 3.2425, and the price of gold immediately rose to 126 shillings and 10 pence per ounce, an increase of 11.5 pence from yesterday, exactly equal to the unprecedented high price of December 8th last year.

National News Agency Dispatch from Paris, 24th: After the news that the US government decided not to suspend the war debts due on December 15th reached here, it immediately caused painful impressions among the French. However, newspapers are still trying to downplay the importance of the matter, apparently fearing that it will have a major impact on France's financial position and the position of the Herriot cabinet. France owes the United States war debts totaling 6,850,000,000 gold dollars under the 1926 agreement, to be repaid in 62 years, including a principal of 3,865,000,000 gold dollars. The principal and interest payable in this fiscal year are 60,000,000 gold dollars. The interest payable on December 15th of this year is 19,261,432.50 gold dollars, and the interest payable on June 15th of next year is 19,261,432.50 gold dollars and the principal is 21,477,135 gold dollars.

Lausanne Conference to Be Reconvened 91

National News Agency Dispatch from Paris, 23rd: Former Finance Minister Flandin has returned after consulting with the British government on the war debt issue in London. According to his statement to the press, if the United States refuses the application of various countries to revise the method of repaying political war debts, then Europe must reconvene the reparations conference and revise the Lausanne Agreement. If the United States refuses to extend the moratorium period for war debts, then the entire issue will have to be reconsidered, because the Lausanne Agreement clearly stipulates that the United States intends to allow the revision of the existing debt repayment agreement.

Reuters Dispatch from London, 24th: British newspapers commented that if the United States insists on paying the debts when due, then no matter how other debtor nations cope, Britain must grit its teeth and repay the debts quickly. However, the difficulties ahead are also generally recognized. The debts due on December 15th amount to £28 million for the UK, and an additional budget will be necessary, equivalent to an increase of 5 pence per pound on income tax. At the same time, France may demand the lifting of the Lausanne Agreement, as French Finance Minister Flandin said in a speech in Paris that there may be a need to reconvene the Lausanne Conference. The Daily Mail reported that if the situation is not handled properly, it will become a long-term source of trouble between Europe and the United States. The Times stated that if Britain does not fulfill its debt obligations, all debtor nations in the world will follow suit, and even private debtors will have an excuse, and the consequences will be unimaginable. Several newspapers advocated that Britain repay the debts in gold, as the only way to avoid major disruptions in the foreign exchange market.

Reuters Dispatch from London, 23rd: Chancellor of the Exchequer Chamberlain said at a dinner party today that some people believe that the British government's previous note to the United States regarding the war debts owed to the United States in December and the uncertain outcome of this note is one of the reasons for the weakness of the pound exchange rate. It should be known that there is no reason to be anxious now. Britain's request for a temporary suspension of payments while the British and American governments discuss this matter is not an unreasonable proposal. The suspension of reparations agreed upon at Lausanne has immediately had a stabilizing effect on European public opinion. A temporary suspension of exchange rate fluctuations is now necessary for the whole world, and the trust created by the Lausanne solution should not be disrupted at the beginning of discussions. He believes that discussions are actually beneficial to both sides. Britain has already repaid £130 million in short-term debts. Britain's trade balance has increased by £86 million compared to the beginning of this year, and the position of the British Empire is also gradually improving, which shows that the temporary fall in the value of the pound need not be a cause for concern.

Reuters Dispatch from London, 23rd: The British side, in debt to the United States, considers President Hoover's war debt declaration to be satisfactory. President Hoover considers Britain's request not to be unreasonable, but says that the debtor nations have not yet explained the facts that payments should be temporarily suspended. It is generally believed that the US President's remarks are quite pertinent, so it is expected that Britain will send another letter to the United States detailing these facts and reasons. The British believe that there are many such facts and that they are very powerful, because if the debts are paid as scheduled, the exchange rate will fluctuate, the economy will be disrupted, capital will flow out, and general trust will be lost.

Understanding Reached on Korean Budget Plan

Reuters Dispatch from Tokyo, 24th: After Korean Governor-General Ugaki and Prime Minister Saitō reached an understanding on the Korean budget plan for next year, Ugaki departed for Seoul this afternoon.

Also, regarding the Korean rice issue, I have consulted with Prime Minister Saitō and Colonial Affairs Minister Nagai, who have agreed not to treat it as foreign rice. The border security issue has also been discussed in various ways, and as a result, it is planned to increase the number of police officers by ○○, which is expected to require a budget of about one million yen."

=The Jichang and Jihai Railways Have Been Repeatedly Destroyed, Making Train Traffic Impossible=

=Attacking Changchun, the Puppet Capital, Causing Panic and Inflicting Heavy Losses on Japanese Troops=

丨The Volunteer Army is Devoting Efforts to Recruitment and Liaison丨

丨Therefore, Unity is Growing Stronger and Momentum is Increasing丨

Special Dispatch from Tianjin: Chuan Dianchen, Commander of the Independent Seventh Detachment of the Northeastern National Salvation Army, is leading the First, Second, and Third Divisions to operate in the Jichang and Jihai Railway areas. The number of times the traffic on these two railways has been disrupted is unknown. Commander Chuan is extremely familiar with the terrain. His attacks are like sudden storms, and his retreats are as elusive as sunken fish or lost geese, causing the Japanese and puppet armies to exhaust themselves chasing him. The following is an excerpt from the reports of Gao Yunzhang, Political Special Commissioner, and Wang Mengpin, Military Special Commissioner, of the detachment: 1. On September 18, our army occupied the Jihai Railway and inflicted heavy losses on the puppet army, causing significant damage to bridges and rails. To this day, the entire line remains closed to traffic. Liu Jingchun, Commander of our First Division, and Sun Tiemin, Deputy Commander, returned to the headquarters in Koukou Mountain on the Jihai Railway on the morning of October 2. The division's defense area covers approximately 240 li around the Fourth District of Panshi County, including Maling Station, Hulanji, Changzhen, Heixionggou, Heishizhen, Liujiadian, and Shaoguojie in the Third District. Lin Guiyi, Commander of the Second Division, returned to the Koukou River headquarters on the Jihai Railway on the afternoon of the 2nd. The division's defense area covers approximately 185 li around the Sixth District of Yongji County, including Shuanghezhen, Dongzhan, Xinglongjie, Badaogou, Xinglongchuan, Huashuhezi, Weitanggou, and Dahechuan, Nanxiangshihezi, Huangqibao, Jinjiatun, Yilaxi in the Fifth District. Li Ziyang, Commander of the Third Division, led his troops in battles against the Japanese and puppet armies in the Songjiagou and Yaojiagou areas along the Jichang Railway, without a fixed defense area at the moment. Around 5 PM on the evening of the 2nd, Zhao Furui, Brigade Commander of the 25th Brigade of Feng Zhanhai's army, led his troops and 6,712 recruited bandits to Koukou River in Yongji County, requesting to be reorganized into the National Salvation Army and to be under the command and dispatch of Chief Supervisor Zhu Jiqing. This unit had strong men, well-fed horses, and well-equipped weapons and ammunition, including four heavy machine guns, two light machine guns, and 21 boxes of ammunition. (Note: Brigade Commander Zhao's unit was made up of those who defected from the garrison troops at Zhangjiawan, Xiaohaozi, and Mihezi stations along the Hachang Railway.) It was agreed to introduce this unit as the Independent Eighth Detachment of the Northeastern National Salvation Army. On the 4th, the unit marched in formation to Xinanbao and recruited 1,410 members of the local self-defense force, further strengthening its strength. 2. On the 6th, the headquarters of the Seventh Detachment advanced to Koukoukou in the Third District of Panshi County (on the Jihai Railway) and established contact with Song Guorong's army of the Eighth Route of the Fourth Military Region in Liaodong (Song was a defector from the garrison troops in Panshi County). Because Song's army had already recovered Shuangyang County (100 li south of Panshi County), that day, Brigade Commander Xie Zhensheng of the Fourth Military Region in Liaodong came to present six rockets for shooting down Japanese aircraft. On the morning of that day, Ma Junshan, Chief of Staff of our Eighth Detachment, came to Chalukou to report on the recruitment of the Xinanbao Self-Defense Force in the Fourth District of Shuangyang County and requested that our Military Special Commissioner Wang Mengpin go to inspect and reorganize them. However, Wang had already advanced with the headquarters of the Seventh Detachment, so Political Special Commissioner Gao Yunzhang accompanied Chief of Staff Ma to Xinanbao to inspect the First and Second Divisions and the machine gun company. On the evening of the 7th, the Eighth Detachment ordered an advance. On the 8th, Wang Hailou, Commander of the First Division of the detachment, led his troops to Zhujiadatun, 20 li south of Changchun. Zhu Pengjiu, Commander of the Second Division, led the machine gun company to Matoutai, 25 li from Changchun. On the evening of the 9th, they attacked Changchun, causing panic in the puppet capital. The Japanese and puppet armies defended with all their might. In order to preserve their strength, our army changed its target and attacked the Gongzhuling Station and Fanjiatun Station on the South Manchuria Railway. On the evening of the 10th, they engaged in a fierce battle with the Japanese and puppet armies, killing over 100 enemies and injuring many more. At dawn on the 11th, enemy reinforcements arrived and attacked our rear with armored trains. The Eighth Detachment was surrounded and fought fiercely until noon before breaking through a bloody path. Both sides suffered considerable casualties. 3. Temporary maintenance committees were established in the areas recovered by the Seventh and Eighth Detachments to: 1. Maintain local order; 2. Provide military rations. The security responsibilities were assumed by the garrison troops in each area. As for the offices of the political and military special commissioners, they were temporarily not established due to economic reasons and were located within the headquarters. 4. On the 11th, over 1,000 Japanese soldiers departed from Jilin on track-mounted armored vehicles to Shuanghezhen to protect the repair of the railway that had been destroyed by the Seventh Detachment. Our Second Division immediately engaged them. After a stalemate of half a day, our Second Division retreated to Qiaomailing due to strategic considerations. The Japanese army then intensified the repair work and extended it to Heixionggou that night. A trainload of soldiers also arrived from Jilin. Our First and Second Divisions jointly ambushed them. After fierce battles for two days and three nights, the enemy's corpses piled up like pillows. At dawn on the 14th, due to the depletion of ammunition, we ordered a retreat to Sanjiazi, 20 li from Yantongshan. The headquarters returned to Koukou River. In this battle, over 100 enemies were killed, and the number of wounded is unknown. We captured one light machine gun and 61 rifles. Our army lost 27 men and injured 60. The consumption of ammunition was 10,315 rounds. On the afternoon of the 14th, the First and Second Divisions and the machine gun company of our Eighth Detachment retreated to Guanli, Shaoyantun, Guojiatun, Bajiazi, and other places west of Yima River (105 li from Changchun and 35 li from Chalukou) to rest and replenish. 5. On the morning of the 15th, the headquarters of the Seventh Detachment posted proclamations to inform the farmers to quickly harvest their fields, with proper protection provided by the garrison troops in each area, and to provide the farmers with horses to speed up the harvest. On the 20th, the entire Jihai Railway was opened to traffic under the protection of the Japanese army. However, passenger and freight trains were still frequently ambushed by our army, so there were few passengers. On the 27th, the puppet state's rebel army of Zhang Haipeng's Seventeenth Regiment (Huang Regiment), Eighteenth Regiment (Han Regiment), and Fifteenth Regiment (Qin Regiment), as well as the First Brigade of the Jilin Garrison (Brigade Commander Zhang Junzhe is Zhang Haipeng's eldest son), arrived at the key stations on the Jihai Railway, forming a confrontational posture with our Seventh Detachment. On November 1, after the Eighth Detachment had completed its reorganization and replenishment, the headquarters moved to Koukoubao. We believed that since the Eighth Detachment had disregarded sacrifices and repeatedly defeated stubborn enemies since the start of the resistance against Japan, and since the frontier was already cold and the roads were covered with ice and snow, the soldiers were mostly wearing single-layer clothes and shoes. If there were no consolation, they would inevitably feel disheartened. Therefore, we sent Military Liaison Officer Wei Minggao with a letter to Koukoukou at Xinanbao to borrow 2 million strings of Jilin official notes (equivalent to 4,000 silver dollars) to reward the soldiers and encourage them. On the 2nd, the joint office of the political and military special commissioners of the Seventh and Eighth Detachments was established at Koukou River, with three sections: General Affairs, Military Affairs, and Propaganda. The General Affairs Section was divided into four units: Documentation, Dispatch, General Affairs, and Accounting. The Military Affairs Section was divided into two units: Organization and Training. The Propaganda Section was divided into an Editorial Unit and a Propaganda Team. There were also two confidential secretaries. On the 4th, Staff Officer Tian Zixin of the Kou Kou Detachment and Li Zhihe, the leader of the Propaganda Team, were dispatched to contact Luo Mingxing's army (nicknamed "Three Rivers Good") along the Jichang Railway, preparing to take action simultaneously in Jilin and Changchun at an appropriate time. 7. Staff Officer Tian and Team Leader Li returned on the 7th to report that Luo's army was willing to comply with the agreement and hoped to be reorganized into the National Salvation Army to jointly resist Japan. 6. The Seventh Detachment has now expanded to over 47,000 men (including over 14,000 men recruited from Liang's army [nicknamed "Dou Mountain Good"], over 1,500 men recruited from Zhang's army [nicknamed "Golden Mountain Good"], and many other small groups of three to five hundred men). The Eighth Detachment has not expanded since the Battle of Gongzhuling and currently has over 8,400 men. On the morning of the 7th, the Seventh Detachment received a report from Vice-Adjutant Lu Xudong of the First Regiment of the First Division that a regiment of rebel troops stationed in Shuanghezhen on the Jihai Railway was advancing towards Chalukou. After receiving the report, an emergency meeting was immediately convened, and it was decided that: 1. If we encounter troops who had been forced to surrender to the puppet state but are now returning to the fold and willing to cooperate with us sincerely, we should consider it carefully and act according to the situation to prevent a feigned surrender. 2. If we discover that the advancing troops have Japanese soldiers covering their rear, we should immediately attack them head-on, regardless of the circumstances. After the vote, Zhu Pengjiu, Commander of the Second Division of the Eighth Detachment, was ordered to lead his troops to the rear line and occupy positions in the Nanxiangshihezi area of the Fifth District of Yongji County, with the machine gun company providing cover for the left and right flanks. Liu Jingchun, Commander of the First Division, was ordered to take the second line and occupy positions in Erdaogou. The Seventh Detachment was to serve as a reserve force. At 10 AM, over 100 enemy vanguards were led by Adjutant Liu to seek an audience with Commander Zhu, claiming that "our army is ordered to proceed to Shuangyang. We are all Chinese, and we hope to be allowed to pass through." Commander Zhu generously agreed to their passage. However, as the main body of the enemy troops entered our defense area, they suddenly opened fire. Little did they know that our army was well-prepared. Their cunning can be said to have been a self-inflicted wound. Over 500 men were disarmed, and over 200 men from the mortar company were captured. According to the prisoners, they were the Fifteenth Regiment under the command of the rebel Zhang Haipeng, ordered to create disturbances under false pretenses. At dusk, 500 to 600 Japanese soldiers advanced towards our army under the cover of light machine gun squads. Commander Zhu ordered the machine gun company to flank the enemy's rear and sent a detachment of infantry to lure the enemy forward. When the enemy advanced to a position 5 li from Nanxiangshihezi, they fell directly into the machine gun company's position. Commander Zhu immediately ordered the machine guns to open fire. The Japanese soldiers were caught off guard and, due to their unfamiliarity with the terrain, fell into a heavy encirclement. Only two or three out of ten managed to escape. In this battle, our army captured four light machine guns, 15,225 rounds of ammunition, and 406 rifles. Our army suffered no deaths and over ten injuries. At 9 PM, another meeting was convened to: 1. Extend the defense line; 2. Dispatch personnel to establish close contact with friendly forces in the vicinity; 3. Request the general chamber of commerce to allocate weapons and ammunition. On the 11th, Propaganda Officer Wang Zuofei and four others were sent to establish contact with friendly forces. Political Special Commissioner Gao Yunzhang, together with Staff Officer Tian Zixin of the Eighth Detachment, went to the Jichang Railway to contact Luo Mingxing's army again and then proceeded to the headquarters to request assistance. (November 22)

Visiting Feng in the Northern Frontier

Feng Strongly Advocates Using Force to Recover Lost Territory 94

Dispatch from Zhangjiakou: Feng Yuxiang recently published a telegram, expressing his opinions on the current situation, which has attracted nationwide attention. Yesterday, our reporter made a special trip from Ping to Zhang to learn that Feng is residing at the old site of the library on Tuergou South Street, while Feng's entourage is living at Aiwulu on Tuergou North Street. The reporter first visited Feng's Secretary-General Wang Yiyuan at Aiwulu, who then introduced him to Feng on South Street. Feng's residence is in the middle of the street. A copper plate with the inscription "Feng's Residence" hangs on the black door. There is only one gatekeeper. The reception room is inside the gate. A long table in the room is used to serve tea to guests in earthenware teapots. Feng lives in three rooms in the north, with his wife and children. There is also a separate study room. When Feng received the reporter, he was wearing an old Zhongshan suit made of coarse blue cloth, with cloth-covered buttons in the middle, and a short sheepskin coat. His appearance was the same as before, but his hairline was mostly white. The following is a record of the conversation:

(Reporter asked) Will you attend the Third Plenary Session of the Central Committee? (Feng answered) In the past, many resolutions have been proposed at the previous Second Plenary Session, or the titles of the proposals have been read aloud once. In my personal opinion, the resolutions should be implemented once they are passed. As for whether I will go to Nanjing to participate or not, I have not yet decided. (Asked) If you do not attend the Third Plenary Session, do you have any proposals? (Answered) I have several proposals that I am preparing to draft. The first proposal is to recover the lost territory by force, because I have always advocated using force to recover the lost territory. Without using force, there is no way to recover it one day. The Shanghai 19th Route Army's defeat of the Japanese army is an example. Second, I also have proposals on military affairs. (Asked) Since you moved to Zhangyuan, there have been many rumors from the outside world. What are your thoughts on this? (Answered) I received a telegram from Minister Luo earlier and sent a telegram to question him. He replied that it was a telegram from Jiang Zuobin from Japan. When I received Mr. Luo's telegram, I was very surprised, but after a long time, I remembered that people always add a crime to me. If they don't say I am a communist, they say I am a restorationist, so I sent out the Jiang telegram. However, when I opened the newspaper, I saw that many parts were omitted. Now I have opinions, but I am afraid that when I tell you (referring to the reporter), I will see the words "omitted." (Asked) What is your future plan? (Answered) Our ancestors left us a few words, teaching us to endure hardship and constantly think about revenge. Unexpectedly, some disappointing people have no concept of enduring hardship. Instead, they are lying down and taking their salaries. Isn't that infuriating? My future plan is to use force to save the country and endure hardship to do it. (Asked) What are your thoughts on the Northeastern Volunteer Army? (Answered) Recently, I heard that there is a local gentleman in Heishan County named Sun Hongyou, who is already in his eighties. Because of his resentment towards the Japanese invasion, he destroyed his home to help the country and summoned the Volunteer Army to fight against the Japanese army. The Japanese army later used a large force to suppress them. He led the Volunteer Army to Xinlitun and continued to resist. It is truly admirable and respectable for an old man in his eighties to do this. Others, such as Ma Zhanshan and Zhu Jiqing, are all fighting in the snow and ice. I have already sent letters to comfort them. (Asked) What are your criticisms of the League of Nations? (Answered) I have begun to write a report criticizing the investigation team, which will be published before the League of Nations meeting. (Asked) Will you be leaving Chahar recently? (Answered) I have decided not to leave this place for the time being. The rumors of going to Shandong or Guangdong are not true. After the conversation, the reporter said goodbye. It is said that Feng's daily life is mostly spent reading and learning foreign languages, and his mood is still quite relaxed. (20th)

Liu Xiang Attacks Xufu Again

Deng, Tian, and Liu Issue Joint Telegram to Cease Fire 95

Dispatch from Hankou: Liu Xiang launched a heavy attack on Luzhou and Fushun. After a bloody battle for ten days, Liu Wenhui's troops resisted stubbornly, making it difficult to capture quickly. When a conflict occurred between Liu Wenhui's and Tian Songyao's armies in Chengdu, Liu Wenhui, to avoid being attacked from both sides, specially withdrew the defending troops from Luzhou and Fushun to the Minjiang River basin to coordinate with both sides. On the 18th, Liu Xiang's army occupied Fushun, Neijiang, Gongjing, and Zigong. On the 21st, it also occupied Luzhou. Liu Xiang had solemnly stated to Deng Xihou, Tian Songyao, Yang Sen, Liu Cunhou, and others when he launched the second general offensive that he would withdraw his troops immediately after Luzhou and Neijiang were captured and would never prolong the war. This time, after Luzhou and Neijiang were captured, Liu Wenhui's army retreated far away. Liu Xiang suddenly dispatched Pan Wenhua, Tang Shizun, Wang Zhiyi, and other troops to take advantage of the victory and attack Xufu, occupying Jiang'an on the left and Rongwei on the right, advancing towards Xufu, no more than 100 li from Liu Wenhui's rear. It is now heard that Liu Xiang stated that he must capture Xufu before he can cease the war. Liu Wenhui also stated that he can give up Xufu and retreat to Baoding. Therefore, from the surface, Liu Xiang seems to have an absolute victory, while Liu Wenhui seems to be in a defeated position. However, it is heard that Liu Wenhui's army suffered no losses during the retreat, while Liu Xiang's army suffered great sacrifices in attacking the city. Although he obtained the resources of Luzhou and Neijiang, the vitality was damaged after the destruction. Therefore, the victory or defeat cannot yet be judged in reality.

Deng Xihou and Tian Songyao, although they seem to favor different sides on the surface, have consistent interests and the same policies. However, Deng is more composed among the generals. Since the outbreak of the war, in addition to claiming to follow the central government's orders to mediate by force, he has never expressed his true attitude. When Neijiang and Fushun were occupied by Liu Xiang's army on the 18th, he sent a telegram to all parties on the 19th to call for peace. The telegram stated, "To Superintendent Liu of Chongqing and all division and brigade commanders and commanders of the 21st Army, Superintendent Liu of Suiding and all division and brigade commanders and commanders of the Sichuan-Shaanxi Border Defense Army, Army Commander Yang Zihui of Guang'an and all division and brigade commanders and commanders of the 20th Army, Army Commander Liu Zigan of Chengdu and all division and brigade commanders and commanders of the 24th Army, Army Commander Tian Songyao and all division and brigade commanders and commanders, Division Commander Li Qixiang, and Division Commander Luo Pingzhang, since the outbreak of the Sichuan war, Xihou has repeatedly received telegrams from the central government to mediate and run around to resolve the conflict. His tongue is parched and his lips are dry, but both sides are deadlocked and refuse to yield. As far as Luzhou and Ziyang and as close as the provincial capital, in field battles and street battles, countless people have died. The people have suffered from the swords and spears, and the houses have been turned into ruins. The tragic situation is unbearable to hear. If the purpose is to seek long-term peace and stability in Sichuan, then Division Commander Tang's Outline for Governing Sichuan has been endorsed by all parties. Chairman Liu's Jiang telegram also advocates the same approach. It can be seen that both sides have similar intentions. It is hoped that a meeting can be held to discuss the details and implement the central government's efforts to promote the implementation. Unfortunately, before the cup was opened, the war started. To wage war in order to achieve good governance is to make the people suffer before they can enjoy happiness. Why not first use the law to restrain each other? If the comrades still insist, sanctions will not be too late. At a time when the national crisis is deepening and foreign countries are watching, internal strife is endless, which is a cause for criticism. Moreover, the people of Sichuan are haggard and their vitality has not recovered. Such devastation is unbearable to imagine. Xihou is burdened with a heavy responsibility and the lives of the people are at stake. For the sake of the country and Sichuan, he cannot ignore this. In his earnestness, he appeals for a ceasefire and respectfully asks you to abandon your prejudices and adopt his humble suggestions. On the one hand, order the troops on the front lines to immediately cease military actions. On the other hand, agree on a date for a meeting to discuss the overall plan in detail. The use of force should be the last resort, and negotiation should be the first. The solution should be sought through political means, and war should not be waged in the local area again. The country will be fortunate, and Sichuan will be fortunate. With tears in his eyes, he submits his words and awaits your clear instructions. Your brother, Deng Xihou." But the effectiveness of this telegram is yet to be seen.

In Chengdu, Liu Wenhui's and Tian Songyao's troops fought fiercely for three days and three nights, from the 16th to the 19th. Tian's army suffered slight losses. As a result of Deng Xihou's mediation, Tian's army withdrew from the city. Deng issued a Hao telegram on the one hand and invited Liu and Tian to cooperate on the other. On the 21st, Deng Xihou, Liu Wenhui, and Tian Songyao issued a joint telegram to cease fire. The generals of the three armies issued telegrams of support at the same time. The armies are like clouds and rain, and it is not known when the chaos in Sichuan will end. (23rd)

Local Dispatches

Songjiang 96

People of Fengjing Request Establishment of a Junior High School: The ancestors of Xu Xingtao, a gentleman from Fengjing, donated fields to the public, designating them for the operation of schools. Recently, Xu Xingtao, a descendant, expressed dissatisfaction with the education authorities' poor management, which resulted in a loss of 40,000 yuan in the Songjiang Bank. He submitted a petition to the Education Bureau, stating that his ancestors had donated fields to the Yun Jian Qiu Zhong Jing Xian Three Academies to benefit the scholars and promote culture. Since the reorganization into the Education Bureau, it has been used specifically for education purposes. Now, with an annual rent of about 4,000 yuan, the accumulated funds are quite considerable. If properly preserved and used to establish more schools, the original donors would benefit. However, the authorities deposited the money in the bank, where it was coveted by unscrupulous merchants, who embezzled over 100,000 yuan of education funds. Who is responsible for this disaster? It is heartbreaking to speak of it. At present, Songjiang lacks junior high schools, especially Fengjing. Every time high school graduates are unable to go out, they linger and drop out of school, all because Fengjing does not have a junior high school. Therefore, he requested the Education Bureau to submit a request to the county government to establish a junior high school in Fengjing with the accumulated education funds to prevent the children of Fengjing from being denied access to education.

Nanhui 97

Huinan Elementary School Donates Funds to Help the Volunteer Army: Huinan Elementary School in this county launched a monthly donation campaign to support the Northeastern Volunteer Army. After discussion by all faculty and staff, the following measures were decided: 1. All faculty and staff will donate 5% of their monthly salary. 2. A bamboo tube will be set up in each grade to encourage students to save their candy money and voluntarily contribute. (A settlement will be made every month, and the most generous contributors will be rewarded by the school to encourage participation.) 3. School workers will contribute 2% of their monthly salary. 4. It is also heard that this monthly donation campaign will continue until the lost territory is recovered.

Suzhou 98

Initial Verdict in the Shenjia Bang Tragedy: The Public Security Bureau transferred the case of Ye Guai's false alarm of a fire and robbery in Shenjia Bang, Suzhou, in which police officers and patrolmen shot and killed four firefighters and pedestrians, as well as the discovery of the Red Pill organization, to the local court. After several trials, the verdict was announced yesterday (24th) at 4:30 PM. Patrolman Fang Yuqing was found guilty of manslaughter and fined 600 yuan. Police officers Yao Zengxiang and Chen Zhiquan were each sentenced to one year and two months in prison. Police officer Li Hongzhang was sentenced to one year in prison. Guo Xiangsen was sentenced to one year and six months in prison for manufacturing Red Pills and fined 520 yuan. Zhao Yizhang was sentenced to six months in prison for assisting in the manufacture of Red Pills and fined 60 yuan. All defendants, except Zhao Yizhang, declared their dissatisfaction in court and prepared to appeal after receiving the verdict.

Anti-Japanese Association Defendant Attempts Suicide: Huang Zixin, 99

a member of the Wu County Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, Shi Zhifan, an employee, and Sheng Zhixing, and others were reported by the County Party Department to the court for embezzlement and malpractice. After several investigations by the court, the case was complicated and no public prosecution was filed. Yesterday (20th), the local prosecutor's office summoned Sheng Zhixing and others for another court investigation and ordered them to remain on bail. However, Huang Zixin, an important figure in the case, was an important figure in the Wu County labor community, serving as the labor representative of the County Government Labor Arbitration Committee, as well as the chairman of the woodworking union, and a standing committee member of the Anti-Japanese Association. He felt that he had been falsely accused in this case. Yesterday morning (24th), he secretly swallowed cologne and opium paste to commit suicide. Fortunately, his family discovered it early and urgently summoned doctors Li Guangxun and Zhang Buxiong to save him. He was fortunate to be reborn. After the poisoning, a suicide note was found near him, which has been sent to the local prosecutor's office for filing by his brother.

Lei Renlong Temporarily Granted Bail: Lei Renlong, former 100

magistrate of the Wujin County Court, was accused of dereliction of duty and embezzlement. After investigation by the Wu County Local Court under the order of the High Court, he was sentenced to one year in prison and fined 800 yuan. Lei appealed to the High Court, which scheduled a hearing for 1:00 PM on December 17. Lei Renlong applied for a suspension of detention due to illness. Yesterday (24th), the Criminal Court ruled that he was allowed to be temporarily released on bail with a written guarantee of 3,000 yuan.

Tax Police Chief Inspects Changshu and Returns to Suzhou: Since the 101

Ministry of Finance reorganized the anti-smuggling agency into the tax police, Ling Xichao, the chief of the Fourth District, has worked diligently to handle the tax police affairs of the three counties of Suzhou, Wu, Changshu, and Kunshan. In particular, the ports of Hupu, Luyuan, and Fushan in Changshu are the gateway to the Yangtze River and are strategically important. Most of the distribution of smuggled salt passes through these ports. Therefore, he inspected Changshu yesterday and summoned the officers of the patrol boats under his command to instruct them on the direction of their work. After completing his official duties, he returned to Suzhou by boat yesterday. According to recent investigations, the monthly sales in the district have increased by more than 500 shares. The prosperity of official sales is unprecedented. According to those in the salt industry, Chief Ling is very serious in handling official duties, which is why he has been able to achieve such remarkable results.

Wuxi

Suicide by a Traveler Taking Poison at the Ben Niu Inn on East Lake Road 102

The First Inn, on the evening of the 21st of this month around 10 PM, received a single traveler. He claimed his name was An Fusheng, 30 years old, from Ben Niu. He came from Shanghai to Wuxi. The tea server attended to him, and he booked room number 32. Since he had no luggage, he paid the room fee of 3 jiao and 2 fen in advance. The next morning, he asked the tea server to bring water to wash his face and lamented his misfortune, muttering to himself. He said he had been a tailor in Shanghai but liked to gamble, causing financial difficulties. He had a younger sister who was a prostitute on Fourth Avenue, so he borrowed money from her. However, his sister not only refused but also incited thugs to beat him severely, leaving him covered in bruises. The tea server didn't pay much attention to this. Soon after, An went out and returned around 10 PM the night before last, booking the same room. He asked the tea server for a writing brush, inkstone, stationery, and envelopes, and locked himself in to write. However, by 10 AM yesterday, the guest hadn't gotten up yet. The tea server became suspicious, knocked on the door, and called out, but there was no response. He then pried open the door and saw the guest with a pale face and saliva flowing from his mouth. He was already dead. His bedding was stained with raw opium liquid. It was then realized that he had committed suicide by taking poison. Beside him was a suicide note. Afterwards, Hua Hegao, the manager of the inn, along with the local warden Xi Zhiliang, reported the matter to the county court and requested an autopsy. Prosecutor Shen led officials to conduct the autopsy, confirming that it was indeed suicide by poisoning. After the autopsy, he instructed the warden to prepare a coffin for burial.

Two Robberies in One Day: Burglaries Frequent Despite Winter Defense Efforts 103

Although the authorities are diligently tracking down criminals, it's like walking through thorns everywhere, making it impossible to prevent everything. The day before yesterday, two robbery cases occurred one after another. 1) Hu, the wife of Hua Yinqiao, a resident near the City Orphanage, was carrying two children and going home after shopping at Dashiqiao at 10 AM yesterday when she was robbed of a gold ear pick by thugs while passing by Ba'erfang. Hua Hu shouted loudly to catch the thief. People gathered upon hearing the cries and apprehended the thug, handing him over to the police, who took him to the First Precinct. Officer Qin held a preliminary hearing. The thug confessed that his name was Wang Afu, 28 years old, from Dongmen, and sold firewood for a living. He admitted to robbing the gold ornament. After the confession was verified, the documents were prepared and transferred to the central bureau for further investigation. 2) Yesterday afternoon around 7 PM, two female travelers from Shanghai arrived in Wuxi by train, intending to visit relatives in Jiangyinfang outside the North Gate. While walking near the three-way intersection of the Railway Hotel, they hesitated because they didn't know the way. Suddenly, three thugs approached and asked where they were going. The women replied that they wanted to visit relatives in Jiangyinfang. The thugs, seeing an opportunity, falsely directed them to go east. The women, suspecting nothing, walked near the slaughterhouse next to the railway when the thugs drew weapons, silenced them, robbed them of a gold bracelet and more than ten silver dollars, and fled.

Jiangyin 104

The Farmers' Association Petitions the Province to Abolish Surcharges: The County Farmers' Association, according to a petition from Zhang Yiru, a cadre of the Sixth District Farmers' Association, stated that Jiangyin, bordering the Yangtze River, has poor land and impoverished people. The land price is no more than ten yuan per mu. This autumn, the rice price is low, and farmers are in dire straits. However, the Finance Bureau of the County Government has raised land prices and levied excessive taxes, increasing the mu tax, such as the 5-fen temporary mu tax, the 2-fen grain storage mu tax, and the 2-fen household tax. Surcharges even exceed three times the regular tax, which is truly unbearable for farmers. They specifically request that the Provincial Government be petitioned to abolish these taxes in accordance with the law to alleviate the people's suffering in Jiangsu.

The Military Tribunal Summons Jiang Hong of the County Party Headquarters 105

Last month, he reported that Qing middle school students Li and Jiang Zuyuan had reactionary connections. After investigation by the county, the evidence was confirmed. They were sent to the Provincial Provisional Military Tribunal for investigation. Yesterday (the 22nd), the Military Tribunal, needing to summon Jiang Hong, made a long-distance phone call to the County Party Headquarters, informing them that Jiang Yanghong had gone to Zhenhou for interrogation.

County Principals Petition for Payment of Overdue Salaries in Jiangyin 106

The public primary and secondary schools in the county, because the Education Bureau owes wages for eight months, are on the verge of running out of funds and cannot maintain operations. On the 22nd, they held a joint meeting at the Education Bureau to discuss the matter of the overdue payments. It was decided on the spot that at least three months' worth of salaries should be paid first. The schools previously received tax certificates for the first land price tax of the Republic of China's 21st year issued by the Finance Bureau, which were difficult to cash and suffered intangible losses. They requested that the relevant government authorities prohibit issuing such certificates in the future. After the meeting, the Director of the Education Bureau, Wang Ruo, and the principals of various schools, including Jiang Jingbo, went to the County Government Finance Bureau to petition. After repeated consultations, the Director of the Finance Bureau agreed to raise 15,000 yuan to pay one month's salary to maintain operations.

Local News

Sun Ke's Observations After the League of Nations Meeting 116

▲The League of Nations' Final Measures May Still Involve Sanctions

▲Japan's Withdrawal from the League of Nations Will Not Become a Reality

▲China Can Only Overcome Difficulties if the Government and People are United

The League of Nations convened a meeting this time, but before formally considering the Lytton Report, the meeting was already deadlocked. Seeing that the League of Nations has repeatedly convened meetings without effective measures, China declared its intention to invoke Article 16 of the Covenant, requesting sanctions against Japan. Japan, in turn, threatened to withdraw from the League of Nations. At the same time, there were also issues related to the islands in the South Pacific that the League of Nations entrusted to Japan for administration. As a result, some observers speculated that Japan's attitude was so strong that the Northeast issue could not be resolved peacefully. If the League of Nations implemented sanctions, another world war would inevitably occur. However, Chinese delegate Sun Zhesheng did not think so. The following is a record of Sun's recent observations on the international situation:

Predictions on the League of Nations: Sun, in response to questions from the Xin Sheng News Agency reporter, stated that the interests of European and American countries differed, and their positions also varied. The Northeast issue could have been sanctioned this time, but because Britain and the United States could not agree, and France could not cooperate with Britain, it affected the League of Nations' actions against Japan. The United States first opposed Japan's aggressive policies. When U.S. Secretary of State Stimson issued a declaration that the United States would not recognize the current situation in Northeast China as an accomplished fact, Britain, France, and other countries made no expression. France secretly sided with Japan at the time. Recently, due to the military reduction issue, France has changed its pro-Japanese attitude, but Britain and France still disagree on this issue. Japan also used this disagreement to cope. In addition, there are other disagreements that make it unlikely that the League of Nations will immediately impose sanctions on Japan. According to my observation, the League of Nations' handling of the Northeast issue will likely be delayed and remain unresolved.

Japan Will Not Withdraw: Sun stated that Japan's threatened withdrawal from the League of Nations is unlikely to happen unless the League of Nations takes firm measures that are unfavorable to Japan. Since the League of Nations cannot take unified sanctions, Japan's withdrawal from the League of Nations is not a current reality.

World War II: Sun believes that a second world war is perhaps inevitable, but it will take at least three to five years of preparation. The outbreak of war depends on the United States. The United States is not prepared for war, and it has not completed the warship construction program allowed by the Washington Conference. However, Japan is desperately expanding its naval armaments. Britain is also showing weakness to Japan in the East. At the same time, Britain is constrained by many other issues and cannot do anything. Therefore, although there are rumors of a second world war due to the seriousness of Article 16 of the League of Nations Covenant and the League of Nations' attention to the islands in the South Pacific entrusted to Japan for administration because Japan is about to withdraw from the League of Nations, it is unlikely to become a reality.

The Government Must Have Resolve: Sun concluded by saying that the League of Nations' solution to the Northeast issue is, for the moment, bound to make us pessimistic. However, the only way to cope is for those in charge of the government to make up their minds and work with the people to come up with various methods, such as expanding military preparations and actively resisting, so that military and economic measures are thorough. Only then can we defeat the enemy.

Consuls of Various Countries in Shanghai Mostly Express Goodwill Towards China

Many are Outraged by Japan's Violation of International Conventions 117

According to the Central News Agency, the League of Nations Council has already met to discuss the Sino-Japanese incident. Japanese representative Matsuoka is actively working in Geneva, hoping to shirk Japan's responsibility for violating international conventions in order to achieve its desire for armed aggression. However, the representatives of various countries are well aware of its conspiracy and will severely sanction countries that violate international conventions in order to maintain justice and safeguard world peace. Yesterday, a Central News Agency reporter learned from foreign nationals in Shanghai, excluding those from Britain, the United States, France, and Italy, about the attitudes of other countries towards the Sino-Japanese incident:

Spain: Yesterday, the reporter went to the Spanish Consulate to inquire. Because the Spanish Consul General in Shanghai, Ferrer, was away on official business, Deputy Consul Sarracoechea received the reporter. According to him, Sino-Spanish relations have always been very harmonious. Spain dares to say that it is China's best friend. Since the signing of the Sino-Spanish Commercial Treaty in 1864, the nationals of both countries have abided by the agreements, and no incidents have occurred. Examining the facts of the past can prove that the Spanish government has always expressed goodwill towards China in past incidents. He continued, saying that there are currently more than 700 Spanish nationals residing in China, with more than 280 in Shanghai, mostly merchants and Catholic missionaries. As for the current state of Sino-Spanish trade, it is becoming increasingly close. The export of Chinese goods is better than the import of Spanish goods. According to a survey in the 19th year of the Republic of China, Spanish goods shipped to China were only 57,604 customs taels, while Chinese goods shipped to Spain were 790,649 customs taels. Spanish goods mainly consist of wine, cork, olive oil, and fish, while Chinese goods mainly consist of tea, silk, tin, eggs, embroidery, porcelain, and antiques. Minister Garrido is stationed in Beiping and will be going south soon.

Brazil: According to a spokesperson from the Brazilian Consulate in Shanghai, there are only about 100 Brazilian people residing in China, with about 80 in Shanghai. Although there is no deep interaction between the two countries, Sino-Brazilian relations have always been harmonious. Since the signing of the Sino-Brazilian Commercial Treaty in 1881, the relationship between the two countries has become increasingly close and urgently needs to be revised. Therefore, Minister Velloso will be going south to meet with Foreign Minister Luo to revise the commercial treaty. The Brazilian government has always expressed outrage at countries that violate international conventions.

Sweden: The reporter went to the Swedish Consulate to inquire, but Consul General Lilllehook was being treated at the Lester Chinese Hospital on North Suzhou Road due to illness, so no details could be obtained. However, it was learned that Lilllehook's illness was gradually improving and he could be discharged from the hospital next Wednesday. It was also learned that the Swedish government and people expressed outrage at the Japanese destruction of international conventions and sympathized with China.

Switzerland: Swiss Consul General in Shanghai, Lardy, will be promoted to Charge d'Affaires in China. Although the official announcement has not yet arrived in Shanghai, the increasingly close relationship between China and Switzerland is sufficient proof. There are about 280 Swiss nationals in Shanghai, all of whom are merchants. Various international organizations are located in Switzerland, so the government and people of Switzerland respect all international conventions. Consul General Lardy did not make explicit comments on the Sino-Japanese issue, but his sympathy for China was revealed in his conversations.

Mexico: Mexican Consul in Shanghai Allman is a lawyer and is currently working as a lawyer in Shanghai, so he did not want to comment on everything.

▲Secret Meeting Minutes Obtained from Japanese Person

▲Hope Friendly Nations' Representatives Will Not Be Deceived

The National Lawyers Association of the Republic of China, in response to Japanese representative Matsuoka's rebuttal of Chinese representative Gu's speech, in which he attacked the secret meeting minutes of the Japanese Colonial Affairs Ministry discovered by the association last year, claiming they were fabricated, sent a telegram refuting the claim and urging all representatives to pay attention to the Japanese diplomatic policy towards China in the record. The telegram is recorded below: "To Dr. Gu Weijun, Chinese Representative to Geneva, for transmittal to representatives of all nations: In his rebuttal, Japanese representative Matsuoka cunningly stated that the Tanaka Memorial was a forgery and later said, 'Some Chinese, seeing the success of deceiving foreigners by forging documents, seem quite excited and have produced another forged document called the Minutes of the Meeting of the Japanese Colonial Affairs Ministry.' In order to avoid confusing international public opinion, this association cannot remain silent. The aforementioned secret meeting minutes of the Japanese Colonial Affairs Ministry were obtained by an employee of this association from a Japanese person in Harbin. This is an undeniable fact. How can it be called a forgery? Moreover, the contents of the meeting minutes, which state that Japan's diplomatic policy before the Washington Conference was to use barbarians to control barbarians, using the name of international coordination to have the great powers act as Japan's plainclothes troops in China, and that after the Washington Conference, it was to use Chinese to control Chinese, using the tactic of sowing discord to achieve its goal of hindering China's unification, further proves that the backbone of Japanese diplomacy is none other than deceiving the great powers and invading China. This is a vile and treacherous policy, and they are still using this approach to operate actively in the Far East and the League of Nations. We hope that the representatives of all friendly nations will pay close attention to this, not be blinded by sweet words, and not be intimidated by threats. Then the Far East will be fortunate, the world will be fortunate. Sincerely, Liu Liumin, Jiang Yong, Yan Yinwu, Dai Tianqiu, and Liu Zhejing, Standing Committee Members of the National Lawyers Association of the Republic of China."

Yu Yuan Heng Foreign Goods Store Suddenly Attacked with Bombs and Guns 120

▲Three People Entered and Threw a Bomb that Did Not Explode

▲Two Employees Gave Chase and Were Seriously Wounded by Gunfire

▲Anti-Traitor Group Explains the Reason for the Warning

The Yu Yuan Heng Foreign Goods Store, located in Yenkang Lane at the intersection of Shansi Road and Guankou Road, was originally located on Jixiang Street in the French Concession. Recently, it moved to this location due to the renovation of the buildings there. Yesterday afternoon around 3 PM, three young people suddenly came to the store, one wearing short clothes and two wearing long robes. They entered and asked why an order from a certain number had not been delivered. Then, they took out a bomb from their side and threw it into the courtyard of the store. However, it did not explode. Wu Zhuxian, a store clerk, and Huang Yiyong, an old accountant, happened to be in the reception room. Seeing that the bomb had not exploded, they rashly gave chase. One of the young people who had just exited the gate noticed and immediately drew a pistol, shooting at the two men. Both shots hit, and the men fell to the ground. The three young men then calmly escaped. Seeing that the store clerks had been injured, the store urgently reported the incident to the Zhabei Police Station. They dispatched detectives to investigate. The unexploded bomb was taken to the police station for safekeeping, and the two injured men were taken to Renji Hospital for treatment. It is reported that Wu Zhuxian, the clerk, is 62 years old, from Jiading. The bullet entered from the front of his left leg and exited through his bladder. Huang Yiyong, the old accountant, is 49 years old, from Ningbo. The bullet hit his abdomen. Both men are in critical condition. Because Wu is over sixty years old, his condition is even more dangerous, with little hope of recovery. It is also reported that the store has repeatedly received warning letters from anti-traitor groups in the past few months, alleging that the store is still continuing to sell inferior goods, which led to this disaster.

After the incident, the China National Soul Anti-Traitor Group sent letters to various newspapers, stating their warning letter to Yu Yuan Heng Store: "The owner of Yu Yuan Heng Store knows that you have been found to be selling enemy goods. After several warnings from this group, the store has been deaf and ignored it. This group is using preliminary means to warn you. After seeing this letter, if you still do not wake up, this group will use the final means to deal with you. China National Soul Anti-Traitor Group."

Levying Increased Import Tariff on Foreign Rice

Song Ziwen Is Seriously Considering 121

Yesterday, a reporter had an audience with President Song of the Executive Yuan and inquired about regulating the people's food supply and increasing import tariffs on foreign rice. He provided a detailed explanation of the advantages and disadvantages, which are recorded below. This year, our country has a bumper harvest, and rice prices are extremely low in rice-producing areas. As the saying goes, "cheap grain hurts farmers," so it is urgent to circulate domestically produced rice and increase import tariffs on foreign rice to achieve regulation. I have long been paying attention to this matter. However, if various local taxes and levies on rice transported out of the provinces cannot be uniformly abolished, then regulation will be merely empty talk. What deserves particular attention is that provinces such as Fujian and Guangdong have always been short of rice and rely heavily on imported rice from Annam and Siam to feed their people. If we rashly increase import tariffs on foreign rice, the effect of regulation may not be seen, and a portion of the population will suffer from the impact of restricted sales first. Therefore, the government is carefully considering and planning comprehensively to ensure that surplus rice in rice-producing provinces can be circulated, while rice-deficient provinces are spared from the harm of high rice prices, so as to avoid favoring one side at the expense of the other, etc.

The Mission of Zhou Xunyu and Others 126

Zhou Xunyu, Chief of Staff of the 16th Route of the Liaoning Righteous Army, Zeng Wowo, Chief Counselor, and Liu Shi, Zhang Guowei, and others, carrying official documents from Zhan Taojun, Commander-in-Chief of the Northeastern National Salvation Allied Army, and the calling card of Shi Lingge, Commander of the 16th Route, arrived in Shanghai to report on the situation to the Northeastern Righteous Army Relief Association and request assistance. The original text reads: "Respectfully submitted: Due to the misfortune of the nation and the fall of the Northeast, after years of bloody battles, half of the territory has been recovered. Since our army began the war of resistance, despite all the hardships, our determination to kill the enemy has never wavered. Since swearing an oath, we have led our subordinates, including Ji Handong, Shi Ling, Zhang Wei, Yuan Wu Delin, Wu Zuohua, Zhang Mingwu, Huang Yonghan, and others, a total of more than 43,500 people, in fierce battles against the enemy in the Jinzhou, Chaoyang, Shenyang, and Xinmin areas. Although there are national salvation soldiers and patriotic organizations in the rear, and overseas compatriots are enthusiastically donating, the remote roads make it too slow to provide immediate relief. After repeated consideration, for the sake of national salvation and military convenience, we have specially dispatched Zhou Xunyu, Zeng Wowo, Liu Shi, Zhang Guowei, and others to represent the entire army to enter the pass, present everything in person, and implore you to sympathize with the suffering of our warriors and provide as much assistance as possible, so that our iron-blooded men can have no worries and devote all their efforts to killing the enemy. If the work of national salvation is not abandoned halfway, the recovery of the three northeastern provinces can be expected, and the 30 million people will once again see the blue sky and white sun. We eagerly await your orders."
