Li Fuxun Discusses the Financial Industry of Overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia

Believes It Should Be Rationalized 127

Banking leader Li Fuxun recently sent his daughter to England to study and took the opportunity to investigate the situation of overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia. Furthermore, after the January 28th Incident, overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia provided significant assistance, and the majority of remittances were entrusted to Li for distribution. As an encouragement, he simultaneously represented the beneficiaries in expressing their gratitude. Upon his return, he wrote this to inform the people of the country. The article recognizes that the rationalization of the financial industry of overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia is the key to resolving the economic panic of overseas Chinese, and it is worthy of attention.

The Current Situation of Overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia and the Efforts We Should Make: The activities of overseas Chinese occupy an extremely important position in our country's national economy. For many years, trade has shown a huge deficit, relying on remittances from overseas Chinese to make up the difference. Whenever there are floods, droughts, or famines, overseas Chinese donate generously, and their enthusiastic support during the January 28th Incident, amounting to millions of dollars, is particularly commendable. Therefore, in today's context, to develop the national economy, there is no doubt that we must seek cooperation in capital and talent between the country and overseas Chinese. Southeast Asia is the center of overseas Chinese activity. Overseas Chinese account for more than half of the population of the Straits Settlements, and in Singapore, where its capital is located, overseas Chinese account for two-thirds of the population. In addition, overseas Chinese are scattered throughout the Malay states and the East Indies archipelago, and their numbers are also large. When we travel to various parts of Southeast Asia, there is hardly a place where we do not see Chinese-style buildings. Being in such a place is like being on our own land. In terms of economic power, overseas Chinese own many mines and rubber plantations. Overseas Chinese also occupy the majority of merchants and brokers. Today, Westerners still cannot but give credit to overseas Chinese for the development of Southeast Asia. The reason for this is profound. However, our attention to overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia lies not in their large number and great power, but especially in the depth of their relationship with the motherland. Overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia usually remit tens of millions to 200 million yuan to the motherland, accounting for more than 80% of the total remittances from overseas Chinese. Due to the enthusiastic remittances from overseas Chinese, the Chinese-owned financial industry in Southeast Asia has emerged in response to the times. Furthermore, since the majority of remittances from overseas Chinese are entrusted to Chinese-owned financial institutions, the exchange between Southeast Asia and Hong Kong and various ports in the country is entirely under the control of the Chinese-owned financial industry. We must pay even more attention to the fact that when the powers develop colonies, they often use political and financial power as the vanguard, and industrial and commercial power arises from this. However, our overseas Chinese are able to establish a foundation for industry and commerce with their bare hands and then complete their highest financial power, from a state of no unity and no organization to a systematic economic organization. Under the weak political protection of the motherland, they have established their amazing great achievements. Their spirit of hard work and struggle is truly admirable. In recent years, the world has experienced an unprecedented panic. The main businesses of overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia, namely tin mines and rubber, have both suffered significant blows due to overproduction and plummeting prices. In addition, with restrictions on immigration in various places, the number of overseas Chinese has been decreasing day by day, and remittances to the country have been sharply reduced as a result. The Chinese-owned financial industry in Southeast Asia has been deeply affected. In order to adapt to the environment by forming alliances, the Chinese Commercial Bank, the Ho Hong Bank, and the Overseas-Chinese Bank merged. These three banks all have strong influence in Southeast Asia. Among the three banks, the Chinese Commercial Bank was established the earliest, the Overseas-Chinese Bank had the largest capital, and the Ho Hong Bank was the most prosperous. The main points are listed below:

Year of Establishment Capital Paid-Up Capital & Reserves Deposits

China Commercial Bank 1922 1,000,000.00 1,172,865.78 4,100,90.24.23

Ho Hong Bank 1917 4,000,000.00 20,746,240,.09

Overseas-Chinese Bank 1920 5,250,000.00 656,425.70 8,381,317.95

The above figures are based on last year's financial statements. The currency is the Straits Settlements dollar. Long history, strong capital, and extensive business are all elements for the development of the banking business. Observing the above points, we anticipate that the Overseas-Chinese Banking Corporation Limited, which will be formed after the reorganization, will definitely gather the strengths of the original three banks and eliminate their weaknesses. Therefore, this merger is not only a passive response to the current difficult environment, but also actively sufficient to open a new era for the financial industry of overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia. Its definite and significant benefits are: 1) Monopoly on the exchange between Southeast Asia and Hong Kong and between Southeast Asia and various ports in the country. In the past, due to the same attention to remittances from overseas Chinese to the country, there was considerable competition in business between the three banks. In recent years, due to the reduction in remittances, competition has become increasingly fierce, and business income has decreased. After the merger, remittances will be concentrated, and with the strength of its capital, it will undoubtedly monopolize remittances from overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia. 2) Saving expenses and increasing net profit. According to last year's financial statements, the expenses of the three banks were 117,000 yuan (Straits Settlements dollars, similarly hereinafter) for the Chinese Commercial Bank, 714,000 yuan for the Ho Hong Bank, and 407,000 yuan for the Overseas-Chinese Bank, totaling 1.24 million yuan. After the merger, at least one-third, about 400,000 yuan, can be saved. Therefore, a single item of expense savings can increase net profit considerably. 3) Developing business and expanding influence. The Overseas-Chinese Banking Corporation Limited, which will be formed after the merger of the three banks, will have large capital and the history and status of the three banks. As a result, not only will the loyal customers of the three banks have even stronger faith, but the general public will also tend to trade with it. The progress of business is beyond doubt. After appropriately reducing the original branches of the three banks, it can use its remaining strength to set up business organizations in places where its business influence has not yet reached. The prosperity of the business can be expected. Finance is the key to all matters. If we want to revive the economic power of overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia, we must first make the Chinese-owned financial industry in Southeast Asia stable. In order to consolidate the financial power of Chinese-owned banks in Southeast Asia, in addition to the rationalization of the organization mentioned above, the domestic economic community must provide appropriate assistance. In the financial industry of overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia, the passive

aspect is that the financial business of Southeast Asia must be entrusted to the newly formed Overseas-Chinese Banking Corporation Limited, and there is no need to compete with it. Otherwise, the unnecessary competition between the three banks, which was fortunately eliminated by the merger, will be revived by the domestic financial industry, which will suddenly emerge to compete for the financial market in Southeast Asia. If one wave is not yet smooth, another wave rises. The hard-won merger of several months will be in vain. The harm is small. As a result of internal conflict, both sides will be hurt, and foreigners will reap the benefits. The disaster is great. This is the first thing that must be properly planned between the domestic financial industry and the overseas Chinese financial industry. Secondly, if we believe that the financial business of Southeast Asia is promising, then we may as well buy the shares of the Overseas-Chinese Banking Corporation Limited, which is in the process of being organized. The face value of the shares is 40 yuan, but the current market price is only 20 yuan due to the financial downturn in Southeast Asia. Judging from its assets, it should be worth at least 30 yuan or more. In the future, when the market turns around, the property will appreciate, or the business will develop, it will be worth even more. Purchasing shares worth 30 yuan or more at a price of 20 yuan is a more simple and beneficial way to indirectly participate in the financial business of Southeast Asia than to establish a new business and open branches to engage directly. This purchase of shares directly provides assistance to the financial industry of Southeast Asia, indirectly encourages overseas Chinese, and greatly contributes to the revival of the overall economic power of overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia. This is the second thing that must be properly planned between domestic economic power and foreign economic power. If we can follow this path, the result of domestic and international cooperation will have a great effect on the development of the national economy. Some say that the development of domestic industry depends on foreign investment. Now, advocating investment overseas is not going against the trend? Regarding this point, we must recognize that first, the overseas Chinese economy and the domestic economy cannot be strongly separated. Whenever the Chinese people encounter incidents, they call on overseas Chinese for help, but they discriminate against the current economic panic of overseas Chinese, which is contradictory. Second, overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia already have a solid economic foundation. At present, they have occasionally suffered setbacks. If we can give them a helping hand, the service of overseas Chinese to the motherland in the future may far exceed that of the past prosperous days. It is a light and easy task, and the effect is immeasurable. Third, I believe that it would be better to change our perspective and invest in the overseas Chinese business in Southeast Asia in order to achieve the result of internal and external cooperation, rather than making a superfluous effort to buy real estate, build buildings, and purchase foreign securities in domestic cities. I am not trying to abandon the domestic business of the Chinese people. Thinking of this, I suddenly thought of the domestic financial community, which also suffers from the shortcomings of sectarianism and weak capital. As a result of unnecessary competition, the domestic financial community reduces the benefits it deserves, and the external financial community cannot make sufficient contributions and assistance to the society and the country. If it can adapt to the trend and carry out mergers, the progress of the financial industry in the future is unlimited. The significance of this merger from a national economic point of view is far greater than the merger of the Chinese-owned banks in Southeast Asia.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Telegraphed the Ministry of Finance Requesting That the Export Tax on Northeastern Medicinal Materials Still Be Collected 135

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Finance yesterday, saying: "To the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing, greetings. On the 20th of this month, we received a letter from the Medicinal Materials Industry Association, stating that since the Northeastern customs were blockaded, the government has been levying taxes in other locations. Since the government does not recognize the abandonment of Northeastern territory, it naturally considers the products of that region to be domestic goods. If taxes are to be levied on goods transported from there to Shanghai, it would be fair to only supplement the Northeastern export tax. However, the customs now taxes Northeastern products transported to Shanghai as foreign goods, which is truly inappropriate. Northeastern production of medicinal materials is not small, and we should protest to the customs and request the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to forward this to the Ministry of Finance to facilitate commercial transport.' Based on this, we have investigated that the Northeast is our country's territory, and the people there are naturally our country's people. The products of that region are the source of livelihood for the people there. If taxes are heavily levied, merchants will not be able to profit, and they will inevitably abandon it. How can the people there not worry about their livelihoods? The government values people's livelihood, and it will certainly not abandon the people of the Northeast. For the sake of the people of the Northeast and our country's commerce, we should carefully consider and handle it appropriately so that the people can prosper and the country can become rich. In our opinion, Northeastern products must not be taxed as foreign goods, and medicinal materials, in particular, are needed for people's health and should be subject to low taxes. In addition to protesting to the customs, we are sending this letter to request that your chamber of commerce forward it to the Ministry of Finance, requesting approval to tax Northeastern medicinal materials transported to Shanghai as domestic goods, and to order the customs to comply. Sincerely, etc.' Upon investigation, since the Northeastern customs declared a blockade and levied taxes in other locations, according to the original regulations, only transit taxes were collected on local goods transported from Andong, Niuzhuang, and other places to Shanghai. Only those transported from Dalian to Shanghai were subject to import taxes as foreign goods. Later, a sudden order changed the regulations, and all goods transported from Andong, Niuzhuang, and other places to Shanghai were also subject to import taxes. As a result, soybeans from Dong Province were subject to a tax of 10% ad valorem, sorghum from Niuzhuang was subject to a tax of 80% ad valorem, and cocoon silk from Andong was subject to a tax of 70% ad valorem, which is more than ten times the transit tax, which uses the old Xianfeng tax rates. Based on the request of the industry, the association has repeatedly telegraphed your ministry, requesting that taxes be levied according to the original regulations. More than a month has passed without a reply. The liquor industry, after paying the taxes, has no financial resources, and the increased costs will make it difficult to sell in Shanghai. If they are shelved, the customs will also have to impose fines according to the regulations. As a last resort, they have returned the original goods to Niuzhuang. The situation of other industries is roughly the same. Now, the medicinal materials industry has sent a letter with the same request. We should promptly order the customs to continue collecting transit taxes on local goods transported from Niuzhuang, Andong, and other places to Shanghai according to the original regulations. Otherwise, the lost territory of the Northeast will not be recovered, and the livelihood of the interior will be cut off first. Any planning for the country cannot be done in this way. We earnestly submit this, hoping that your ministry will review it and promptly approve it, which would be for the public good. Respectfully, the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce."

Recent Situation of Wounded Military Officers of the 19th Route Army Remaining in Shanghai

All Will Move into the Civilian Sanitarium 136

During the January 28th invasion of Shanghai by Japanese troops, our 19th Route Army bravely resisted, bringing glory to the country and fighting for the integrity of the nation. Their reputation will forever be recorded in history. However, many officers of the army were wounded in this battle. According to the reporter's investigation, there are still more than 40 wounded officers remaining in Shanghai, more than 30 of whom are staying at the Civilian Sanitarium founded by Chu Minyi, Lin Kanghou, and others. It is heard that the wounded officers of the army believe that the sanitarium's quiet location, fresh air, complete facilities, and dedicated medical services are suitable for recuperation, and all will move into the sanitarium for treatment. Once they have recovered, they will return to their units.

Kidnapped Elementary School Student on Gaun Road Rescued 138

▲ Rickshaw Puller Bravely Chased and Shouted

▲ Two Chinese Police Intercepted the Car Head-On

▲ Two Bandits Captured, Remaining Bandits Fled

▲ Elementary School Student Terrified, Face as White as Clay

Yesterday at around 4:00 PM, a kidnapping case occurred on Gaun Road in the French Concession. Fortunately, the rickshaw puller bravely chased and shouted for help. The bandits' car was intercepted on the spot by two Chinese police officers, and two kidnappers were arrested. The hostage was rescued from the clutches of the bandits. The details are recorded below:

Elementary School Student Zhang Hengfu Zhang Hengfu, a grandson of Zhang Yunjii, a resident of No. 359 Gaun Road in the French Concession, is a 52-year-old Ningbo native who started his career in the hardware industry and accumulated considerable wealth, which made him a target for bandits. Zhang has an eight-year-old grandson named Hengfu, who attends a school on Weihaiwei Road in the Public Concession. He goes to school every morning and returns after school in the afternoon, always transported by a dedicated rickshaw puller. This has become a daily routine.

Five or Six Bandits Arrive At around 4:00 PM yesterday afternoon, rickshaw puller Mao Xiaotao went to pick up Hengfu as usual. Unexpectedly, when he reached No. 353 Gaun Road, only a few steps away from home, five or six bandits suddenly rushed out from the roadside. All the bandits were wearing blue cloth shirts and pants, and their ages were all around thirty. Two of them pulled out pistols to stop the rickshaw puller from advancing.

Taking the Hostage into the Car At the same time, the remaining bandits swarmed forward and beat rickshaw puller Mao Xiaotao. Three bandits took the opportunity to snatch Hengfu from the rickshaw, dragged him into a car parked by the roadside, and one bandit started the engine and drove the car north at high speed. Mao Xiaotao witnessed his young master being kidnapped and bravely chased and shouted for help. The bandits' car turned into Fuli Road, intending to flee east.

Two Police Intercept the Bandits' Car The area was remote, and Mao Xiaotao's shouts for help alarmed the neighborhood. Two Chinese police officers, No. 367 and No. 392, happened to be stationed on Fuli Road and intercepted the bandits' car head-on. However, due to the disparity in numbers, only two bandits were captured. The remaining bandits escaped. The hostage, Zhang Hengfu, was still sitting in the car, but his face was ashen and he was petrified.

License Plate Numbers Were Forged At the same time, Supervisor Jin Jiulin, Detective Li Yaolong, Zhang Ziying, Detective Qin Youyu, Zhang Daorong, Zhang Chunsheng, and others from the special agency of the French Concession police station also heard the alarm and drove to search. They then assisted the two Chinese police officers, No. 367 and No. 392, in taking the bandits' car to the police station along with the arrested bandits. After inspecting the car, it was found that the license plate number 1459 was forged. The real license plate numbers were No. 1092 in the French Concession and No. 9495 in the British Concession.

Two Bandits Confess to Kidnapping The two bandits arrested on the spot were interrogated by the police chief. One bandit, the driver, confessed his name was Yu Haitao, 25 years old, from Tongzhou, residing at No. 340 Huishan Lane, Huishan Road. The other, Lu Heshang, 27 years old, from Tongzhou, residing in a bungalow on Wuzhen Road in Zhabei, worked as a pushcart operator. They directly admitted to gathering people to carry out the kidnapping. Afterwards, Zhao Lianfu (62 years old, from Tongzhou), the owner of the car, was brought from Huishan Lane, but it was heard that he was not involved in the case. The police chief ordered them to be detained separately, pending referral to the court for interrogation.

Abandoning Textbooks, Yun Huifang Willing to Go Through the Pass

Request to Join the Volunteer Army Rescue Team 139

Yun Huifang, the young patriot who used a bomb to warn treacherous merchants, recently, in view of the fact that winter is approaching, animals are hibernating, and the Northeastern Volunteer Army is still fighting against Japan to the death in the snowy and icy land, and the rescue work is urgent, she is willing to abandon her textbook life and go to the Guanwai (area beyond the Great Wall) to implement the rescue work. Therefore, at 1:00 PM yesterday, she went to the office of the Northeastern Volunteer Army Rescue Team in Xiaonanmen Sanmei Temple and requested to join. The team's communication officer, Song Guoguang, received her and told her that the Northeast is a battlefield of artillery fire, and rescue work requires considerable experience and knowledge to be competent, and that she is currently studying hard at Junyi Middle School. The review of the third batch of team members has been completed, and the fourth batch has not yet begun. If there is an opportunity, she will be notified. Yun left her contact information and departed.

Rescue Team Selects Supervisors The Northeastern Volunteer Army Rescue Team yesterday selected Hong Ludong, Lu Jingshi, and Zhu Xuefei as supervisors, Pan Yunchao, Jiang Bocheng, Qi Xuezheng, Ouyang Huizhen, Ge Zhaoji, Liu Youzhong, Sun Kejin, Hong Xiheng, Zhou Lianze, Xu Huiyi, Yang Peiwen, and Yu Yaoqiu as design committee members, and Wu Kaisheng, Wu Youyuan, Yuan Yangan, Pan Zhe, Chen Yufei, Fan Mingnong, Gu Changyuan, Gu Nanqun, and Jin Yanyuan as consultants. Notices have been sent to each, requesting them to take office on a specific date.

Reception Center Donates Woolen Blankets The Jing'an Temple War Zone Disaster Relief Center, considering that the Northeast is bitterly cold and the volunteer army's clothing is thin, yet they are bravely fighting the enemy in the icy and snowy land, their loyalty and courage are commendable and their situation is dire, sent 140 surplus unused woolen blankets donated by various sectors during the January 28th Incident to the Volunteer Army Support Association for forwarding to the front lines.

From the Juelu Hotel to the Yipinxiang 140

▲ A Thief in the Military World, Quite Skilled

▲ Dancer's Coat Not Yet in Hand

▲ Rickshaw Puller and Doorman All Shouted Loudly

▲ Chen Yi Cleverly Arrested in the End

Chen Yi, from Changsha, Hunan, used to work in the military but is now unemployed. Due to economic pressure, he took the risk of engaging in petty theft. Chen usually dresses fashionably and stays in rooms at major hotels, paying attention to the comings and goings of guests. When the opportunity arises, he steals clothing and other items from the rooms of guests who are out. Because of his quick actions, he has never been caught. A few days ago, Chen went to the Juelu Hotel on Xizang Road and opened room number 66. The balcony of that room was connected to room number 17 of the neighboring Yipinxiang Hotel, separated only by an iron railing. One morning at one o'clock, Wang Suzhen (17 years old), a local woman who was a dancer at the Da Hu Dance Hall, and a dance partner Guan Shi were staying in room number 17 of the Yipinxiang Hotel. At five o'clock in the morning, they went out together, leaving a coat in the room. Chen saw this and climbed over the iron railing, entered room number 17, stole the coat, and climbed back over the railing, preparing to return to his room. Unexpectedly, the rickshaw puller Zhang and the doorman of the Yipinxiang Hotel saw him and shouted loudly. Chen panicked and threw the coat into room number 64, trying to evade responsibility. Afterwards, the incident was reported to the Laoza police station, which ordered detective Chen Yonggui to come and arrest Chen. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the first criminal court of the First Special District Court. Police station lawyer Ru Baoqi requested a postponement because the defendant had committed multiple offenses, which had not yet been clarified. Presiding Judge Feng questioned Wang Suzhen and Chen Yi and ordered Chen to be detained pending further investigation.

The Banking Industry's Statement on the Shipment of Silver Dollars to the Northeast

Entirely for Commercial Relations 141

Recently, a large amount of silver dollars has been shipped from Shanghai to the Northeast, totaling more than 8 million yuan in two weeks. This has attracted social attention. A reporter from the New Voice News Agency interviewed a leader in the banking industry yesterday to inquire about his opinion on this matter. According to him, the shipment of silver dollars to the Northeast is entirely for commercial relations. From the perspective of the banking industry, various banks in the city have branches in the Northeast. The people of the Northeast usually trust the exchange notes issued by the banks. Since the establishment of the puppet state, the Japanese have implemented an aggressive policy, hoping to monopolize the economy and force the people of the Northeast to use Japanese banknotes. However, the people still prefer to use Chinese banknotes. However, the banks must have sufficient reserves for redemption to prevent emergencies. In addition, now is the time when soybeans in the Northeast are being exported, and cash is also needed. In addition, there are many other telegraphic transfers to the Northeast, so it is necessary to ship silver dollars for adjustment. In short, the financial community firmly believes that the shipment of silver dollars has absolutely no other relations.

Songjiang Natives in Shanghai Appeal for the Songjiang Newspaper

Telegram from Song Bao Seeking Assistance 142

The Songjiang Song Bao newspaper, due to publishing news about the Anti-Japanese Association's inspection of goods, was deemed by the Party Headquarters to have violated Party orders and was ordered to cease publication. Songjiang natives residing in Shanghai yesterday sent a joint telegram to the Central Party Headquarters, the Provincial Party Headquarters, the Provincial Government, and the Political Affairs Office, requesting rectification to uphold public opinion. The original telegram is recorded below: "On the 20th of this month, the Songjiang Anti-Japanese Association inspected enemy goods and distributed leaflets, creating a commotion that led to conflict. Yuanda & Co. closed its business on the same day, and the citizens were in a state of unrest. The news spread to Songjiang and Shanghai, and the facts are clear. However, the Songjiang County Party Headquarters, because the Song Bao published news about the Anti-Japanese Association's inspection of goods on the 21st of this month, deemed it a violation of central secret orders and sent a letter to the county government ordering it to cease publication. This is deeply shocking. We have always lacked sound public opinion in Songjiang. Since its publication, the newspaper has maintained a position that is barely satisfactory. However, it has been envied by powerful figures because it advocates fairness. This time, the publication of the above news was based on facts. Even if there were errors, according to the regulations for inspecting propaganda, it should be corrected or reprimanded. However, the Party Headquarters does not interfere with the Anti-Japanese Association's distribution of leaflets, but considers the newspaper's reporting a violation of Party orders and orders it to cease publication. This cannot help but be suspected of stifling public opinion. In order to protect public opinion, the central government has clear stipulations. As leaders of the people, Party Headquarters should not abuse their power or act impulsively. Fellow Songjiang natives residing in Shanghai feel a deep connection to their hometown and cannot remain silent. Therefore, we respectfully request that your departments and offices quickly rectify this situation in order to uphold public opinion. This is for the public good." Respectfully, Zhou Bingjun, Qu Guannan, Yu Wenwu, Zhu Mengwei, Gao Xiaohong, Zhou Yuwen, Luo Shizhen, Wang Cengzhi, Li Xingcheng, and others from the Songjiang Public Association in Shanghai kowtow.

The Song Bao telegram states: "To all newspaper offices and news agencies nationwide, please be advised that since our newspaper began publication last year, we have earned the false praise of society and incurred the jealousy of those in power due to our independent stance and impartial commentary. We have been slandered and harmed numerous times. This time, the Songjiang County Party Headquarters, using the excuse of Party orders, ordered our newspaper to cease publication on the 22nd of this month. Under such oppressive power, where is there justice? Our newspaper is now sending a telegram to the province requesting relief. We hereby send this telegram to all fellow countrymen, hoping for your assistance. It would be fortunate for our newspaper and fortunate for the world of public opinion. All members of the Songjiang Song Bao kowtow."

Cai Wuji, Director of the Product Collection Office for the Chicago Exposition Preparatory Committee, Returns to Shanghai 143

Cai Wuji, Director of the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry and concurrently Director of the Product Collection Office for the Chicago Exposition, went north on October 26 for matters related to product collection. He stayed in Tianjin for three days, discussing product selection with the Tianjin Commodity Inspection Bureau and other organizations. It was decided that coarse and fine furs, dried and fresh fruits, and specialty products from Hebei Province would be collected by the Tianjin Inspection Bureau and other agencies. On the 2nd, he traveled from Tianjin to Beiping, where he held discussions with Mayor Zhou Da-wen, Director Wang Shen of the Public Works Bureau, Director Cai Yuan of the Social Affairs Bureau, Chairman Leng Jiaji of the Beiping Chamber of Commerce, and others regarding the purpose of the Chicago Century of Progress Exposition, the significance of China's decision to participate, the progress of preparations, the situation of product collection, and his hopes for this trip to the north. Mayor Zhou and others immediately expressed their enthusiasm and support. The next day, at the Chamber of Commerce, Chairman Leng invited representatives from forty industries, including carpets, cloisonné, and lacquer carving, to discuss the matter of Beiping products participating in the exposition. Fearing that the merchants were stuck in their old ways of thinking and did not understand the truth, Cai repeatedly stated that the association would be responsible for compensating for any damage or loss of products. The representatives agreed to select their best products and concentrate them at the Chamber of Commerce in mid-December for shipment to Shanghai. Cai also believed that this Chicago Exposition valued drama, so he made a special trip to Daren Hutong to visit Mei Lanfang. They talked for a long time about the participation of dramatic performances in the exposition. Mei was also very interested in being invited to North America again. At noon on the 14th, at the invitation of Mayor Zhou, he again consulted with Mei Lanfang, Qi Rushan, and others, and they felt that there were economic difficulties. Finally, Mei agreed to further plan for funding when he came to Shanghai at the beginning of next month. The preliminary work for industrial, artistic, dramatic, and scientific products from various places in Beiping and Tianjin has been completed, and Cai has returned to Shanghai in recent days.

Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau Mediates Labor Dispute at China General Edison Company Yesterday 144

▲Both Parties Willing to Resolve the Issue Themselves Outside

▲If There is No Result, Mediation Will Be Held Again on the 28th

After the workers of China General Edison Company resumed work, the Social Affairs Bureau mediated the dispute at 10:00 AM yesterday. The company requested a postponement because Chairman Wang Yiting was in Luoyang. After persuasion, the mediation was officially held at 2:00 PM in the afternoon. Labor representatives Fu Chongde and Hu Yida, capital representatives Zhang Xiaoliang and Gu Qingyi, Zhou Lianze, the Chief of the Civil Training Section of the Municipal Party Headquarters, and Jin Zhongjian, a staff member of the Second Section of the Public Security Bureau, attended, and Wang Gang, a staff member of the Third Section of the Social Affairs Bureau, presided over the meeting. Jiang Baofu was the recorder. Zhu Xuefan and Li Yongxiang from the General Labor Union, Lu Bohong, the manager of the company, and Tan Honglin and Zhang Zhendong from the labor union were also present. First, the chairman reported on the handling of the case. Then, the labor representatives stated the reasons for their four standard demands (see previous report for details): (1) Why are workers not given wage increases when employees are given wage increases? (2) Employees have better treatment and higher wages than workers. (3) The company has had profits in previous years, so increasing wages would not have an impact. (4) If business suffers losses and employees' salaries are reduced, the workers are also willing to reduce their wages. Then, the capital representatives stated that there are 218 workers with wages above 40 yuan and 538 workers with wages below 40 yuan. If the workers' proposed standards are followed, the company's expenses would increase by more than 100,000 yuan per year, which is impossible to accept. The reasons are: (1) across-the-board wage increases are a bad precedent; (2) the demands are extravagant; (3) the reasons are insufficient; (4) the net profit has already been distributed; (5) prices are falling. After repeated persuasion by the chairman, two methods of increasing wages were proposed: (1) for those with a monthly wage above 40 yuan, and (2) for those with a monthly wage below 40 yuan. The labor representatives made a concession, proposing an across-the-board increase of 8 yuan for workers with wages below 40 yuan and 7 yuan for those with wages above 40 yuan. The capital representatives stated that the time for this mediation was limited and that they did not have time to hold a board meeting. A decision could only be made after the board of directors discussed the matter. As a result, for the sake of cooperation, both labor and capital voluntarily agreed to try to resolve the issue themselves outside. The chairman approved the self-resolution and scheduled another mediation for the 28th. The meeting adjourned around 5:00 PM.

Extension of Railway Coal Transportation Price Increase Continues for Three Months 145

Regarding railway transportation prices for coal and coke, the National Mining Federation has repeatedly petitioned the Ministry of Railways to reduce prices to lower costs and prevent the dumping of foreign coal. The Ministry of Railways believes that the high cost of domestic coal is due to other reasons, and the level of transportation fees has little impact. Furthermore, the cost of railways is also crucial, and no further reductions can be allowed. However, in order to promote production and sales, the case of suspending the price increase has been extended repeatedly. Now, the third extension is due to expire on the 20th of this month. The Shanghai Coal Industry Association has specifically petitioned the Ministry of Railways to continue reducing the railway transportation price of domestic coal by 20% in order to prevent dumping and provide relief. Yesterday, a reply was received from the Ministry of Railways, extending the period by another three months. The original approval stated: "We have received your report. In order to consider the difficulties of merchants and encourage the production and sales of domestic coal, this Ministry has issued a notice to all railways to extend the suspension of the price increase for coal and coke transportation by another three months. In addition to separate orders, this approval is hereby issued for your information."

Citizens on Nanjing Road Refute Shanghai Municipal Council's Telephone Price Increase 146

The Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Concession, believing that the residents within the concession are misunderstanding the telephone price increase, published an article in various newspapers on November 18 to defend the company. Now, it is learned that the Nanjing Road Business Association and the First District Citizens' Association have published an article yesterday to refute it. The original text states: "Having read the section on the telephone price increase published by the Municipal Council in the newspaper on the 18th of this month, much of it represents what the telephone company has said or wants to say. This one-sided view is difficult to convince. We hereby refute it as follows: (1) The statements 'the company has not paid dividends since its establishment,' 'although prices have been increased, it is still losing money,' and 'various losses' all belong to the company's own policy of improving services to society and developing its foundation, which users are not responsible for. If one insists on quickly making a profit and recouping investment within 'a period of 26 months' to make a profit, it is not something a public transportation telephone company can dream of. Spring planting and autumn harvest are natural. To sow in the spring and want to harvest in the summer is to blame the sower for being too anxious, not to blame the land for being infertile. The meaning of the fourth paragraph is roughly: 'From August 5, 1930, when the company was established, to the end of September of this year, a total loss of 218,432 taels was incurred over a period of 26 months.' Even in terms of the 26 months of losses, it is natural that the Shanghai Telephone Company has suffered losses due to its efforts to expand its lines to more than four times their original size. This cannot be used as a sufficient reason for a large price increase and retroactive compensation for the new price. Now, the company wants to recover huge sums of money in a short period of time and wants the current 30,000 users to bear the burden of the equipment for 100,000 users in the future (the company also admits this in its reply). This is truly a manifestation of the company owner's excessive greed and is illogical. (2) Regarding the price increase in the 1929 Anthon report, according to his statement, he admitted his mistake, so it has lost its basis. If Anthon were to come to Shanghai again to investigate the recent situation, he would probably also think that such a large increase should not be made suddenly. The above two points are only the most important ones. In short, the Municipal Council is the municipal organ of the Public Concession and should clarify its position and take fair measures. It must not use the arguments of a commercial telephone company as its own words as a municipal authority. This association, as a group of citizens and merchants who pay huge taxes within the concession, has the responsibility to convey public opinion. We hereby offer our advice again, hoping that the municipal authorities within the concession will eliminate prejudices and resolve the opposition to the telephone price increase well to avoid the worsening of social disputes," and so on.

The City's Financial Situation This Year

Deficit Exceeds 500,000 Yuan 147

Since the war, Shanghai's financial revenue has decreased, and expenditures have increased sharply due to post-war expenses. The difficult situation has been repeatedly reported in this newspaper. Yesterday, reliable information from the Finance Bureau stated that at the end of last year, the city treasury had already incurred a deficit of more than 1.1 million yuan. The deficit is even more severe today. From July to October of the 21st year, the total revenue was about 2.7 million yuan, and the total expenditure for various expenses was about 3.2 million yuan. The difference results in a deficit of more than 500,000 yuan. As a result, various methods are being tried to raise funds, and the officials are busy coping with the situation all day long. Even if the future reconstruction public bond is successful, it is all designated for reconstruction in the disaster areas and cannot be diverted. The only plan for now is to live within our means and strive for austerity. It is estimated that even with efforts to collect taxes, the actual revenue in the tax collection area will average about 600,000 yuan per month. It is already difficult to cover the monthly recurring expenses (such as the recurring expenses of various agencies, various coordination fees, and the municipal bond fund), which are all essential expenditures. Therefore, the only way to cope is to implement the principle of using current revenue to cover current expenses in order to barely maintain the current situation. The city treasury deficit will have to be made up after the central government approves the implementation of land tax collection.

County Bureau Issues Notice for the Collection of the Second Installment of Land Value Tax

Deadline Expires on January 24th Next Year 148

The Shanghai County Government and the County Finance Bureau issued a notice yesterday stating that the second installment of land value tax for the 21st year should be collected from November 25th of the lunar calendar, with a deadline of two months. After January 24th of the lunar calendar, a late fee of one-tenth of the regular provincial and county tax will be added. The upper fields and wetlands in the 16th, 18th, and 21st baos must pay the regular provincial and county tax and the additional commutation silver of 6 jiao and 3 fen according to the order of Fengsheng, a collection fee of 2 fen and 7 li per mu. Also, according to the case, a road construction donation of 5 fen per mu, a security group donation of 4 fen, a land survey fee of 1 jiao, and a party affairs fee of 3 fen will be collected. The total cost of the upper fields is 8 jiao, 7 fen, and 7 li per mu. The quasi-regulations in the 24th and 26th baos, require the payment of 6 jiao, 6 fen, and 5 li of regular provincial and county taxes and the additional commutation silver. The collection fee is 2 fen and 85 hao, the road construction donation is 5 fen per mu, the security group donation is 4 fen, the land survey fee is 1 jiao, and the party affairs fee is 3 fen. The total cost of the quasi-regulation fields is 9 jiao, 1 fen, 3 li, and 5 hao per mu. In addition to distributing easy-to-understand leaflets and maps to various industry bundles, the notice is hereby posted to the people and households in the county so that they are all aware and pay the required amount on schedule. Ensure that you obtain receipts and avoid delays that may lead to forced collection. Be sure to pay attention to this notice.

Second Trial of the Anhui Relief Dispute Case Today 150

I await your arrival and look forward to your reply. Quan Shaowu bows respectfully."

Commander Sakonji Departs Shanghai. Commander Sakonji of the Third Fleet of the Japanese Navy has been ordered to be promoted to Commander-in-Chief of the Sasebo Naval Base. Five Provinces and Cities Jointly Manage Highways 152

▲Highway Conference to be Held in Nanjing

▲Shanghai has Sent Tan Boying as a Committee Member

For the purpose of developing highways, the five provinces and cities of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Nanjing, and Shanghai jointly initiated the establishment of a traffic committee for the mutual connection of automobiles in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Nanjing, and Shanghai. Six organizations, including the National Economic Society, the Jiangsu Provincial Government, the Zhejiang Provincial Government, the Anhui Provincial Government, the Nanjing Municipal Government, and the Shanghai Municipal Government, are responsible for the project. The Shanghai Municipal Government has appointed Tan Boying, the Chief of the Fourth Section of the Public Utilities Bureau, as a committee member to attend the meeting. Yesterday, a reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency specifically inquired with Mr. Tan Boying, who said that the matter is still in progress and that committee members have not yet been appointed everywhere. Only this city has appointed him as a committee member. Now, after all parties have appointed committee members, a meeting will be held in Nanjing to discuss the draft and other matters related to highways. This committee is responsible for the management and improvement of highways in the five provinces. In the future, provinces such as Hebei will also participate, forming a seven-province highway committee. As for the highways in the five provinces, they are currently under construction in succession and are expected to be completed in a short period of time.

Painter Chen Tianxiao Prepares to Hold a Personal Exhibition on National Crisis

Chairman Lin Sends Letter of Encouragement 153

The painter Chen Tianxiao, who is skilled in the six methods of painting, has a long-standing reputation. He does not adhere to ancient methods but develops his personality, expressing complexity with simplicity, using a powerful brush, and especially excelling at ink blending. He is not afraid of turbidity in thick ink and is not afraid of dryness in light ink. His few strokes are naturally unrestrained. He is truly a famous work of the modern freehand school. Recently, Mr. Chen, feeling the urgency of the national crisis and lamenting the suffering of the northeastern compatriots, is holding a personal exhibition on the national crisis, selling tickets to help the northeastern refugees. It is scheduled to be held for three days, the 26th, 27th, and 28th, at the Ningbo Fellow Association. It is reported that Mr. Chen recently went to the capital to sketch for the exhibition. Important figures from the central government praised Mr. Chen's works for their powerful style and vigor, calling them rare in modern times. Chen Guofu, Chen Shuren, Zhu Jiahua, Shao Yuanchong, Chu Minyi, Wu Zhihui, Xiao Jishan, Wang Qi, Huang Jichen, Shi Ying, Zhang Renjie, and Hong Ludong all personally inscribed plaques to commend and praise him. They also selected and collected paintings from Mr. Chen. Chairman Lin of the National Government sent a letter to Mr. Chen, highly commending him, which is a precedent for Chinese artists receiving preferential treatment from the government and is especially honorable. The letter is recorded in brief below: "Mr. Tianxiao, your selling of paintings to help disaster relief is a manifestation of benevolence and grace, and I greatly admire you. Your mastery of the six methods is excellent and has a long-standing reputation. Bringing harmony to disaster will further enhance your reputation and secure a seat in the art world," and so on. He also plans to personally inscribe a plaque and select paintings from Mr. Chen. Mayor Wu Tiecheng of Shanghai and other celebrities also praise Mr. Chen's works for being extraordinary and exquisite in brush and ink and are competing to order many paintings from him. At the opening, there will be a unique scene.

China and the United States Plan to Establish an Automobile Factory

Ministry of Industry Replies to the Road Association's Letter 154

The China National Road Construction Association sent a letter to the Ministry of Industry requesting the notification of provinces and cities to promote the imitation of automobiles and the development of petroleum. A reply has been received, informing that an automobile factory is being planned with the Ford Motor Company, and petroleum is also being planned for extraction. The Minsheng Factory, which was originally the Liaoning Mortar Factory, has been moved to Tianjin to continue operations. The original letter is as follows: "Gentlemen, We have received your letter requesting the notification of provinces and cities to promote the imitation of automobiles and the development of petroleum. We greatly admire your insights. The establishment of automobile factories and the extraction of petroleum mines are all urgent matters that should be planned and prepared. However, due to the lack of raw materials, economic resources, and talent, we have not been able to implement them. We are currently in discussions with representatives of the Ford Motor Company of the United States to first establish an automobile assembly plant. Once a plan is agreed upon, it can be realized. In the future, we plan to gradually establish manufacturing plants and promote them in various places. The extraction of petroleum is also being planned. Furthermore, the Minsheng Factory, which was originally affiliated with the Liaoning Mortar Factory, has now been moved to Tianjin and renamed the Beiyang Machinery Factory to continue operations. Last month, we received a request to forward a report to the Ministry of Finance to exempt the imported materials from taxes, which has been forwarded accordingly. The above is the reply to your letter. Please be advised. Minister Chen Gongbo."

The Weather in Shanghai Turned Warm Yesterday 155

Since the beginning of winter, Shanghai has experienced two periods of severe cold, with the temperature on the Fahrenheit thermometer dropping close to zero. Unexpectedly, the weather suddenly turned warm in the past two days, especially yesterday, with the temperature rising to 72 degrees. Pedestrians on the road changed into lighter clothes, as if it were spring. However, it is very humid in the room, and there may be severe cold again.

The Tianjin Maru Collides with a Yellow Sand Ship

The Association Submits a Report to the Shipping Office to Order Compensation 157

The boat owned by Lu Zhenxing of the Lu Yu Ji Sand and Gravel Transportation Company in this city, loaded with 50 tons of yellow sand, was sailing past the Changqi Wharf at about 7:00 AM yesterday when the Japanese-owned Dalian Kisen Kaisha's Tianjin Maru was entering the port. The bow of the ship was heading diagonally toward Pudong and speeding, intending to turn around and dock at the Huangpu Wharf on the Puxi side. Therefore, it blocked the Huangpu River and proceeded directly towards Pudong. It did not blow a horn and continued to speed recklessly, disregarding the danger. At this time, it was high tide, so the yellow sand boat could not avoid it and was violently hit by the ship. The ship and cargo sank completely, and the workers on board fell into the water at the same time. Fortunately, they were rescued by the water patrol. The losses were huge. In addition to reporting to the water patrol station, a report was submitted to the Coal and Stone Barge Industry Association, requesting a report to the Shipping Office of the Customs to order compensation. It is reported that the association will send personnel to negotiate with the Dalian Kisen Kaisha today, demanding compensation for all losses.

Public Concession Detectives Illegally Search the Hongshun Mutual Aid Association

The Taxpayer Association Sends a Letter to the Municipal Council Requesting Investigation 158

The Public Concession Taxpayers Association sent a letter to the Municipal Council yesterday stating that they had received a letter from the Shanghai Hongshun Mutual Aid Association, which stated that at 3:50 PM on the 12th of this month, a person claiming to be detective Feng Xueze, accompanied by a Westerner who looked like a public official and a Chinese person in plain clothes, carrying pistols, escorted two women to the association's office in Yongxiang Lane at the intersection of Donghan Laili Road and Zhoujiazui Road to conduct a search. When asked about the reason for the search and whether they had a court warrant, they did not answer. The association's staff members realized that they could not reason with them and could not resist, so they had to let them do as they pleased. However, they searched up and down without finding anything and then left. Afterwards, the association sent personnel to the Jiuxing Road Police Station to inquire about the matter, and it was stated that no one had been sent to conduct a search. They also asked the police station to call the Hongkou Police Station to inquire, but they also said that they knew nothing about it. Upon learning this, they were extremely shocked. However, for the sake of caution, at 10:00 PM that night, they sent personnel to the Hongkou Police Station to inquire and happened to see a Westerner sitting there who seemed to be the one who had come to the association to conduct the search during the day. When asked, he admitted it, but he was vague about the reason for the search and whether he was acting under orders. The association has been registered with the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau and the Party Headquarters as a formal charitable organization. They have been subjected to such illegal violations for no reason. Where is the so-called legal protection for residents, public, and private organizations in the concession? Even according to the regulations of the Police Department, if a search is necessary, the police station should first request a search warrant from the competent court or show the warrant with a bailiff before entering the room to execute the search. Even in the case of a person caught in the act or an emergency, the reasons must be explained. It is absolutely forbidden to do so arbitrarily without reason. The people who came did not have badges, did not state the reasons, and did not follow the regulations. They illegally entered the association's office to conduct a search. Fortunately, the staff members were patient. Otherwise, if they had resisted according to the law, the consequences would have been unimaginable. In such a situation, not only the reputation and legal interests of the association are at stake, but the contempt for legal authority and the infringement of the people's peaceful residence cannot be tolerated. If this practice is allowed to continue, the consequences will be endless. The association has no choice but to report the situation.

We should request that the association seriously negotiate with the Municipal Council to ensure that the detectives apologize in the newspaper and guarantee that the same situation will not happen again in the future. This will not only benefit the association but also allow all residents of the concession to live in peace and avoid harassment.

▲Telegraphic Request to Chairman Chiang for Relief

▲Separate Telegrams to the Central National Government for Negotiation

Autopsy Report on Yao Xiaoji, Kicked to Death by Koreans 160

Koreans Li Changlian and Gui Xichang previously caused a dispute at the intersection of North Sichuan Road and Oujia Road when buying baked sweet potatoes from an elderly woman, Yao Chen, from Changshu. They kicked her two sons, Yao Meimei and Yao Xiaoji, in the abdomen, sending them to Tongren Hospital. Subsequently, Yao Xiaoji died from his injuries. The Public Security Bureau sent a letter to the District Court, requesting that Prosecutor Yang Qi be appointed to conduct an autopsy. The autopsy revealed that Yao Xiaoji died from being kicked in the lower abdomen. However, Dr. Tenggong of the Fukumin Hospital, appointed by the Japanese consulate, refused to participate in the autopsy, claiming that Yao Xiaoji's abdomen had already been dissected, making it impossible to determine the cause of death. Therefore, the Japanese consulate did not punish the two Koreans. The deceased, Yao Xiaoji, was unable to clear his grievances. After Chief Prosecutor Lou Ying of the District Court carefully reviewed the case file, he decided to send a letter to the Public Security Bureau, requesting that Yao Xiaoji's coffin be sent to the Zhenru Forensic Research Institute for a detailed autopsy. At nine o'clock the morning before yesterday, the institute opened Yao Xiaoji's coffin and dissected the body in detail. The autopsy was completed yesterday, but the determination of death caused by kicking still requires pathological tissue and microscopic examination. After all examinations are completed, an appraisal report will be compiled and sent to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for forwarding to the Japanese consulate for negotiation. Yesterday, the coffin was returned to the Fifth Precinct of the Fifth District for safekeeping, and a letter was sent to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for reference.

Shanghai and Jiangsu Authorities Plan to Build the Qingpu-Shanghai Highway 164

The Qingpu-Shanghai Highway is the only major transportation route connecting Qingpu County and Shanghai City, with a total length of approximately 22 kilometers. About half a kilometer of it is within the territory of this city. It is now reported that the road construction project within Qingpu County is currently being bid on and started by the Qingpu County Construction Bureau. As for the part within this city, it is reported that the Municipal Government considers that if the construction of the section within this city is not carried out simultaneously, the project will inevitably lose its effectiveness when the county completes the construction. As for the matters concerning the acquisition of land, the Land Bureau has been ordered to prepare in advance.

Actor Sentenced for Smoking Opium 165

Li Xinpei, a famous actor from Tianjin, also known as Li Liqing, has been performing as an old male role at the Tianchan Stage. At 8:30 PM the day before yesterday, his residence at No. 307, Huile Lane, Yunnan Road, was suddenly searched by Chinese detectives Song Bingzheng and Chen Yaoting from the Narcotics Department of the Public Concession Police, acting on a search warrant from the First Special District Court. At that time, Li was lying on a couch, smoking opium. He was immediately arrested by the detectives. At the same time, Shanghai women Yang Gendi (17 years old) and Li Suzhen (18 years old) were also in the house and were also arrested. It was found that the women seemed to be prostitutes, but they denied it at the police station. At that time, an opium pipe, two lamps, two bowls, twelve and a half taels of opium, and an opium ledger were seized and taken back to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the First Special Court's Criminal Division 1. The police lawyer Ru Baoyi prosecuted Li for providing premises for opium smoking under Article 10 of the Anti-Opium Law and for smoking opium under Article 11. The two women were prosecuted under Article 11 of the Anti-Opium Law. Subsequently, Western Inspector Bai Po submitted a report on the circumstances of the search, stating that when they entered the house, Li Liqing and Li Suzhen were sleeping in the same bed, with an opium pipe placed beside each of them. Yang was sitting on a stool. When Li saw them arrive, he threw two opium pipes out of the window. After they went to find the pipes, they had already been picked up by someone. Only two broken bowls were recovered. One of the pipes presented to the court today was found elsewhere. Li Xinpei confessed that the opium paraphernalia were relics left by his late father, and he sometimes used them when he had a heart attack, and he did not run an opium den. The two women were his students learning opera. The two women confessed that they were learning opera at Li's place and did not go there to smoke opium. Li hired lawyer Zheng Wenkai to defend him. Judge Feng Shide of the Criminal Court reviewed the confession and sentenced Li Liqing to one month's imprisonment and a fine of 120 yuan, with a bail of 500 yuan during the appeal period. The two women were acquitted, and the opium paraphernalia were confiscated.

Yang Shengyuan Acquitted

Wu Yinting's Lawsuit Rejected 166

The Ford Tobacco Company previously entered into a contract with the Gongxing Tobacco Stack in Hangzhou to promote "Lion Cat" cigarettes, stating that mildewed cigarettes should be exchanged, and each empty pack could be exchanged for one cigarette. Gongxing sold over 800 boxes of the brand, receiving gifts and exchanging mildewed cigarettes worth approximately 30,000 yuan. Because Ford refused to pay, Gongxing deducted the amount from the cigarette price of 41,000 yuan. The Ford manager, Wu Yinting, suddenly lured Yang Shengyuan, the manager of Gongxing, to Shanghai on the pretext of inviting him to join Ford as a shareholder. On one hand, he reported to the Old Zhabei Police Station, falsely claiming that Gongxing had ceased operations and that Yang Shengyuan had defrauded him of the cigarettes. The police sent detectives to detain Yang and escort him to the First Special District Court, where he was granted bail pending trial. Later, Wu reported to the police, claiming that Yang had falsely used Ford's name to open a current account at the Zhejiang Industrial Bank to obtain illegal benefits. At a subsequent hearing, Yang's lawyer, Chen Tingrui, explained that the reason for opening a current account at the Zhejiang Industrial Bank was to use public bonds as collateral, and the funds were purely for Ford's use. Later, because Wu Yinting did not submit the accounts for inspection, Yang refused to join as a shareholder, and the current account was abandoned. He also presented letters from the Hangzhou Tobacco Industry Association and the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, proving that the Gongxing Tobacco Stack had never closed down and that Wu Yinting had completely fabricated the facts. The court realized that the plaintiff had indeed made false accusations. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhang opened the court and announced that Yang Shengyuan was not guilty and dismissed the plaintiff's incidental civil lawsuit.

On May 26th of this year, at the home of Cai Dianwu, a farmer in the northern countryside of Huaian County, bandits named Cai Dianzu and Cai Dianfu, etc., went to rob him of 1,020 silver dollars and clothing. Before leaving, the bandits also kidnapped a total of six people, including Cai Dianwu's wife and children. After repeatedly extorting large sums of money without success, they tore up the tickets of all six kidnapped people one after another. In the end, only one person was released after being wounded in the waist by the bandits. After the case occurred, the county government repeatedly ordered its subordinates to pursue and arrest the perpetrators. After committing the crime, the bandits came to Shanghai to hide. Recently, the Huaian County Government found out about this, so it sent Zhi Xiaoshun, the captain of the Mounted Patrol Squadron of the Public Security Bureau of Huaian County, along with detectives Zhang Yadong, Liu Naifu, Cui Tinggui, Duangui, and Gao Congjin, to Shanghai to arrest them. Yesterday morning, the detectives received a tip that the bandit leaders Cai Dianzu and Cai Dianfu were hiding in a bungalow in Zhangjiabang, Wusong. At around 9:00 AM, the captain went to the address and arrested Cai Dianzu. Cai Dianfu had already escaped. The captured bandit was taken to the Seventh District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau for questioning. Since the case was a serious case involving tearing up tickets, he was ordered to be handed over to the original detectives to be taken back to the Huaian County Government for investigation. When the bandit arrived at the North Station, he was questioned and stated that he was 31 years old, from the northern countryside of Huaian, with deeply sunken eyes and a rather fierce appearance.

Recently, he was treated by Dr. Chen Xianzhis, an eye specialist who graduated from the UK, at the Pingleli intersection of Xizang Road and Erma Road. After using a newly invented corneal surgery several times, the white opacity was completely removed, the redness and swelling were immediately reduced, and he was able to see the light again. He is truly worthy of being a master ophthalmologist.

Indian Old Eye Doctor: Indian eye doctor Alin Baxi has been practicing medicine in China for more than 30 years. He graduated from a famous medical school in India and has a physician's business license issued by the Shanghai Municipal Government. All kinds of eye diseases can be cured immediately and without any pain after being treated by him. The address of the clinic is at No. 562, North Henan Road.

Labor Bureau of the Public Concession Recruiting Medical Officers 175

The Health Department of the Public Concession Labor Bureau is now planning to recruit one Chinese assistant medical officer. The candidate must possess medical and surgical qualifications equivalent to those of a registered physician within the concession, be proficient in English, and be able to speak Shanghainese and standard Mandarin. The age should be under 30 to be qualified. Those selected must first undergo a physical examination and serve a probationary period of six months. Only those with satisfactory results will be formally employed. The initial salary will be approximately between 200 and 300 yuan, depending on qualifications, with regular increases thereafter. After 20 years of service, the salary can be increased to 650 taels per month. After three years of service, if the performance is good, a contract can be granted, entitling the employee to benefits such as savings, pensions, and medical expenses. After five years of service, upon the recommendation of the Director of the Health Department, the bureau may provide assistance to facilitate further advanced studies. Applicants must personally submit a written application detailing their qualifications and experience, along with three copies of recent supporting documents, to the Director of the Health Department's office at Room 130A, upstairs in the Labor Bureau Building, 16 Hankou Road, before December 15th of this year. Applicants will not be interviewed, and any attempts to influence the selection process will result in the disqualification of the candidate.

Weather Report 177

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the Shandong coast is clear with intensifying northerly winds. The Yangtze River basin and coastal areas south of Ma'anshan Island will experience cloudy skies with variable winds and localized fog. High altitude areas around are affected by cyclones, due to a low-pressure system moving towards the east-northeast. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in Shanghai was 72.1 degrees and the lowest was 59.7 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest temperature was 71.1 degrees and the lowest was 52.2 degrees.

[L< Standards for Kindergarten and Elementary School Curriculum Promulgated by the Ministry of Education (7)

I. Physical Education Objectives 181

1. To develop the functions of the internal and external organs of children's bodies to achieve proper overall development.

2. To comply with children's inherent love of games, develop their motor skills, and cultivate the habit of taking exercise for entertainment.

3. To cultivate children's personal qualities such as courage, agility, endurance, honesty, fairness, and cheerfulness, as well as the spirit of sacrifice, service, cooperation, and mutual assistance.

II. Types of Activities 182

1. Games. 2. Dance. 3. Exercise (including imitation exercises, skill exercises, apparatus exercises, ball games, track and field, simple martial arts, etc.). 4. Sports meets and game competitions. 5. Swimming (only if adequate facilities and instruction are available). 6. Other activities such as posture training and competitions.

III. Key Tasks for Each Grade Level 183

First and Second Grades

Games

1. Singing games

2. Story games

3. Chase games (including carrying people games)

4. Imitation games

5. Competitive games (such as jump rope, beanbag, etc.)

6. Mud games

Dance

7. Movements to music

8. Simple folk dances

Exercise

9. Imitation exercises

10. Walking, mountain climbing, etc.

Other

11. Posture training

12. Warm-up exercises

Weekly Time: 150 minutes 105 minutes

Third and Fourth Grades

1. Chase games

2. Competitive games (such as jump rope, etc.)

3. Competitive games

4. Imitation games

5. Mud games

6. Folk dance

7. Imitation exercise

8. Skillful Exercise

9. Simple ball games

10. Track and Field

(1) Sprint (2) Long jump (3) Throw (4) Standing long jump (5) High jump

11. Walking, mountain climbing, etc.

12. Posture training

13. Warm-up exercises

Weekly Time: 150 minutes 105 minutes

Fifth and Sixth Grades

1. Competitive games (such as jump rope, beanbag)

2. Competitive games

3. Mud games

4. Folk dance

5. Ball games

6. Track and field

7. Apparatus exercises

(1) Various jumping methods on low and high frames (2) Mud exercises

8. Swimming

9. Hiking, mountain climbing, etc.

10. Posture training

11. Preparatory exercises

Weekly Time: 180 minutes

Appendix

1. Extracurricular sports should focus on activities learned during in-class exercise time.

2. There should be group exercise and individual free activities every day outside of class.

3. Football and basketball should be used by older children.

IV. Key Teaching Points 184

1. Efforts should be made to expand physical education facilities as much as possible.

2. The selection of physical education materials should be based on the child's body, age, and level of technical skill, and must be suitable for the child's psychological, physiological, and living needs.

3. The materials used in the classroom are best aligned with extracurricular activities, so that children can apply them in practice after learning. If children know in advance where they will be applied, they can work harder during learning.

4. Both teaching materials and methods must focus on interest and must take into account morality, preventing hypocrisy, fraud, pride, and the discovery of all bad habits.

5. Natural activities for children, such as running and jumping that do not harm children's bodies and school order, should not be prohibited, and should be promoted to develop children's alertness and speed for activities.

6. Children's games inherent in China, such as "kicking shuttlecock" and "building houses," should be promoted as much as possible. The children's games inherent in the local area should also be selected and promoted as much as possible.

7. China's inherent boxing and other martial arts can also be selected as teaching materials for senior grades at the appropriate time and place.

8. Preparatory exercises, such as lining up, marching, turning, and changing ranks, should not exceed five minutes for lower grades, six or seven minutes for middle grades, and seven or eight minutes for upper grades each class time, and should be natural and not mechanical.

9. For two or more grades, if daily timed assembly exercises (such as morning exercises and afternoon exercises) are adopted, the time should be short, and the teaching materials should focus on imitation exercises.

10. Games and sports should quickly divide and organize children according to their strengths and hobbies, and teachers should provide guidance and assistance, or participate in a certain group movement.

11. Children should be encouraged to maintain good posture. Posture competitions should be held, posture inspections should be conducted once a week, and daily attention should be paid to inspections during children's writing and other homework. Monthly and semesterly settlements should be made to compare the advantages and disadvantages of groups or individuals. Teachers should also pay attention to maintaining good posture at all times to serve as a model for children.

12. Appropriate test methods should be adopted, such as McCloy's "Motor Skills Standards," to examine children's grades and whether they have improved due to physical development, and to enable children to know the degree of progress and work hard to learn. Teachers can also review the effect of teaching and seek improvements in teaching methods.

13. Depending on the school's situation, a sports meeting should be held once each semester or year. Sports meetings are divided into two types: 1. Individual unit. 2. Group unit.

14. Lower grades focus on individual or group competitions in jump rope, shuttlecock, ball, ring toss, beanbag toss, batting, building houses, rolling iron hoops, ping pong, etc.

15. Guide children to record physical development so that children can strive to develop their height and weight appropriately.

Schools Subsidized by the Labor Bureau Must Focus on Cleanliness 190

At the meeting of the Education Committee of the Public Concession Labor Bureau on the 16th, the Director of the Health Department submitted a detailed report on the sanitary conditions of the Chinese schools receiving subsidies. Among them, the sites of five schools were particularly unsuitable, and it was considered that the subsidy funds should be used to find new sites. After discussion, a committee member said that when the sub-committee considered granting subsidies in the past, although they felt that the cleanliness of several schools was not very satisfactory, they suggested granting subsidies because they were the only schools in that location. All the members also believed that it might not be easy for all schools to get satisfactory houses, but the previously established stipulation that the cleanliness should meet the rules of the Health Department was actually beneficial to the schools themselves. Therefore, it was decided that the autumn subsidies would be issued as usual, but the five schools in question should be notified that the issuance of subsidies would have to wait until they moved to a satisfactory location, and that the Finance Department should be allowed to urge the Director of the Health Department to issue the subsidy funds designated for construction as necessary, according to the amount used. This resolution has been approved by the Board of Directors on the 23rd of this month.

Inspection of Curriculum in Chinese Middle Schools: A committee member of the Education Committee of the Public Concession Labor Bureau suggested last time that the principals of Chinese middle schools and girls' middle schools should cooperate with the Chinese vice-principals of their respective schools to report the time spent on each subject in each grade every week to the Education Supervisor, who would then report to the committee to inform them of which subjects are taught in English or Chinese, as well as what textbooks are used and what the nationality of the teachers is. With the consent of all the members, the principals of each school were asked to do so, and the same investigation will be carried out in primary schools in each district in the future. This resolution has been approved by the Board of Directors on the 23rd for implementation, and the Director-General explained that the committee members' hope is that the Chinese language courses in each school will be as consistent as possible with the curriculum of national schools in China.

New School Will Change to Flat-Roofed Building: At the last meeting of the Board of Directors of the Public Concession Labor Bureau, a director said that sports fields in various schools cannot be supplied as much as possible. When building new schools in the future, flat-roofed buildings should be built, and the roof should be used as a place for recreation. The chairman of the Education Committee presented this proposal to the committee. The public opinion is to ask the subcommittee in charge of construction to give special consideration to this method when reviewing future new school sites.

Yuyuan Road Playground Closed: The children's playground on Yuyuan Road has been closed because the construction of the new Western children's school in the Western District is about to begin there.

The 20th Anniversary Art Exhibition of the Shanghai Art College Was a Grand Occasion Yesterday 191

The Shanghai Art College, in order to celebrate the 20th anniversary of the school, specially held a large-scale art exhibition starting on the 23rd of this month, which is divided into three locations. The first location is the recent works exhibition of teachers and students of the Art College, and the location is at the school. The second and third locations are exhibitions of famous ancient and modern calligraphy and paintings. The first part is located at the Chinese Society of Arts and Sciences on Aimai Xu Xian Road, and the second part is located at the Mingfu Library on Albert Road. In recent days, the number of visitors to each part has been extremely enthusiastic, and it is truly a scene of crowds of people. The association also issues calligraphy and painting coupons, each coupon is sold for ten yuan, and you can use the coupon to draw lots to exchange for a famous masterpiece at the first exhibition site. Yesterday, those who went to draw lots with coupons were very enthusiastic, and the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau sent Yan Wenkai to check the coupons and seal the ticket boxes to monitor the process. The calligraphy and paintings on display are rare treasures that are not easy to obtain from the outside, such as Zhao Yong's genuine works and famous works from the Yuan, Ming, and Qing dynasties, ten large Chinese paintings by Liu Haisu, and several extremely valuable oil paintings by Liu. Therefore, those who won paintings with a single ticket were very happy and satisfied. It is said that the exhibition of famous ancient and modern calligraphy and paintings will last for eight more days, and the exhibition of recent works by teachers and students was originally scheduled to close today. Now, due to the crowded audience, it has been extended for two more days until 6:00 pm on the 27th. As for calligraphy and painting coupons, they are sold at the exhibition site and in the Shanghai Art College.
